O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, most noble sons, I have completed this book that is the back of the science of medicine, and I have finished it with its fulfillment and by its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is guarded in our region and is subject to all sorts of things, it has perished and been lost, and there remains nothing but the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the error and the vanities, and the ears are closed and the knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive it together with the order of this treatment according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the irons of cautery, and other instruments of the work with the addition of declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters into this that he should master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of all, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of joints, and the movement and resting of them, and also the source of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hippocrates says that with the hand alone is not much, and with work is little; and likewise in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that those who are not familiar with the things mentioned before, if they attempt to perform surgery, may make mistakes and harm people; thus I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon their knowledge and experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish woman who cut into an abscess of the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another case where a stone was removed from an elderly man, and the stone was large; it also took with it a piece of the bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to extract it, and saw the position of the misalignment and the size of the stone, and if one were to cut it, he would die from it.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And another case where a duke of our land who had broken his leg was taken in for care, and with the fracture he also had a wound; and the healer restrained the fracture above the wound with splints for a long time, and did not allow anything to drain from the wound, and thus it remained until the end; and he commanded that it not be moved, and so it remained until the leg was entirely rotten and the foot and it came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to dislocate his leg; and when I heard it dislocated, it was in place and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way to the corruption was already confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop moving through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another method that would crush the abscess and inflame it, and then it flared up due to its lordship's evil.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should only touch it with iron if it is not in a place where one can remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	Therefore, dear son, I advise you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, where he is in many positions; and I will show in each chapter of this book where he has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is important that you keep these things, so that the foolish may not speak evil of you if you take up your arms in battle, and undertake your maladies firmly and steadily, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are saved; and leave behind you the dreadful diseases of grievous sickness; and take away the things that cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen advises in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a seriously ill person, unless you are called a foolish miracle worker.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatment into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and non-fire medical cauteries, and the chapters are ordered from the top of the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and about the irons of cautery, and about everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and about similar things; and the chapters are ordered and about the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the highest to the lowest, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Whenever we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell the quality of each aid and the harm of every kind.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest and most subtle speech and the secrets kept; and because of this many wise men spoke about it and agreed to it, and I do not use too many words because I shorten it.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cauterization helps universally in every kind of matter, whether the matter is hot and moist, or dry and moist.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry weather, they all agreed that the fire cautery was a great help; but others said the opposite: that the fire cautery is only helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite claimed that the fire cautery helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that come from within people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the hot fire, you harden the body.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in all cases, do not interfere except those who have experienced it, and who know from long experience the chapter on cauteries, and the variety of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and space of time; for other constitutions we have no fear, specifically in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the symptoms gathered and agreed on the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my sons, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and greater good than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the first, it is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members if not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from member to another by separating, and bring diseases of great relief to the affected member; and perhaps it is the evil that the first causes harm due to its high heat and because of the goodness of its substance, if there is not excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I found this by experiment and because of the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is above the truth of things; and because I do not like to speak too long, I will tell you only the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it destroys diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they should be done at what time the cautery is to be applied, and if they prick at their base.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is beneficial in all times, because the harm that comes from it is removed by its help; and even more so if the cautery is for necessary pain, short or long, which cannot wait until the greatest harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, my son, as the foolish people do; for to the disease that is healed by cautery there is no return; and they say so because it is not as they think, because cautery is only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries out the humors that are the cause of pain, and is better medicine for its swiftness of value, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes at any time according to the nature of the humor and the body's condition and its power; and they are gathered in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if not cauterize administered in him where there is little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizing with dense for the pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but it has little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine, and it is seen; but they do not believe that cauterizing works after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauterization is one of the main methods of medicine, not according to the intention of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cauterizing instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they only said that it was due to the quality of gold and its high value; and they said that the heat of the cauterization does not cause harm, but I have experienced this and found that it is not true in some people; and a gold cauterizing instrument is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And therefore, when heating a gold instrument, you should not wait until it is hot due to the color of the gold, and has been cooled; and if it is overheated, they put it in the fire; and thus it has enough protection.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of this, we use fire cauterization that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter on the shoulder joint from toe to foot, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is good for moisture and cold on the head, and it is done for two reasons: because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the joint to the ears, and due to many dreams and tooth pain, and throat pain, and in fact for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the hairs are removed by medicinal solution, which changes the head's skin III or IV times, depending on the virtues and age and custom of the hair, so that it can bear suffering; and then restore the head of the hair.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then let him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on top of his knees; afterwards, put the root of your palm above the root of his nail between his two eyes; and when you see blood flowing, then heat the cauterization which is called «olivare», of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply ink to the bone, and by gently pulling and slightly stretching your hand, then remove your hand slowly, and if you see the bone small; and if you do not see it, start the cauterization again until you see the bone as I told you; then take a little silk, and put it in awe and soft cotton inside, and put on the bone, and leave it three hours; then put moist cloth on burn; and let it be healed until the wound is healed; then treat the burn called «tetrafarmaçon» until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old ones said, that the longer one remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should weaken the cauterization so much that a part of the bone is burned away, and then replace what has been burned off from the bone, and then heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others said that one should weaken the cauterization so much above, and to put in as much as one can take away from the bone as wide as the spindle that women put in their hair for the reason that the humors come out freely; and the wound must remain open for a long time; afterwards it must be healed and sewn.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good for everyone, unless in some men where there is a view of fear; and I think that I should leave it; because the affected ones are weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we testify in other members; and indeed when the affected one is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more safe and mild for me, and of this use I work in the following manner.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the main pain comes from chronic conditions and lasts a long time, one should use the remedies of years and pills called "cochie", and cleansing of head and eyes and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have already mentioned, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	If the patient is very sick and has a high fever, and it is not too hot; then cauterize with that fire cautery we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the cauterization on each of the horns to the bone, as we have mentioned before, and using the cautery called "vasselz"; and place the vacuum tubes in the holes; and raise your hand so that you do not see the bone: the pain is much greater in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the cauterization of the horns be more subtle than the one used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	fire cauterization
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease extends to the ear, and the patient is purged by laxative medicines, and the other cures that I have mentioned in the division of diseases are done, but nothing helps: then you should cauterize according to two methods, namely with medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicine is that you hold a piece of iron, and scrape off the skin and the flesh and apply it to the patient as two or three times, and then make a hole in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can replace the piece of iron outside the skin; and when it is replaced, hold it well and tightly and leave it for twelve hours; then remove it and treat further with a bandage, and leave the wound for two or three days; then put on a cotton pad soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of burns until they are healed; and if you see that some medicines are causing harm, which I have written or treat medicines causing harm.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a cloth or it has a little hook, and in the middle a small appearance; and place it on the painful limb, and hold your hand and gently press the iron a little, until half of the hot surface is gone; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and bleed abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on a string and placing it on the limb for three days; then place moistened cotton on the wound, and cure the limb from inflammation until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", apply it at all points, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	If you treat the wound as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned does not cause much pain and does not suffocate the patient, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is cool; and afterwards place it on the limb for a line of half a finger's breadth, and take your hand once, and be careful not to cover the artery and that it does not come near the bone; and guard against dislocation of the jaw when moving, and the nerves should only have regard to the mouth and that spasms do not cause pain, and guard against bleeding from the artery when cut, or when it is cut, with great fear and immediately to that one who does not know, and who is not studied and experienced; and leave the work in this way; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this fire cautery is not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the wound as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauteries that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cauteries that have two knives; and this fire cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear there is pain from cold, and other medicines have been administered and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cauteries which is called "poins", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After carefully scraping all around the ear, where the pain is felt on both sides, and moving it slightly away from the root of the ear as you have signed the direction of the wound; then apply a poultice made of X parts of each ear; after healing the ear, keep it clean.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with caution is only those that move from the gum, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar wounds that come from sores and spittle of animals.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you encounter this appearance of torture that moves from a stream of tears and spurting of blood from the mouth and throat, and does not cease, then it is necessary to cauterize the pain with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a little further from the temple, and the third in the jaw; and put the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make the cautery above a little bit outside the horn of the ear, and another in the temple as far as a little bit; and leave the cautery as long as half of the face is red; and this is the form of the cauteries:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the resemblance of this surgical instrument is similar to what we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit thicker; after care of the wound as I have mentioned before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have mentioned before, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauteries: two on each horn of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the vessel behind the mouth of the stomach; and cure as we have mentioned before.
de litargie	of laziness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, one should give the patient large and modified headache-relieving pills; afterwards, remove the entire top of the malady, and place the mustard plaster on the occipital bone, as written or treated in the plasters; and this is the way of the fire cautery: if you do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is thus healthy, it is good; and if not, make three cautery burns on the head by descending just above the collarbone, and leave a space of one finger's breadth between each burn; and treat as with the others, and if you have seen that it has stopped, and the maladies are suffering, then make one cautery in the middle; and if the work is, two more above the two horns, and treat until he is healthy; and let the cautery called "olivare" be as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head of years and mud that we have previously mentioned; then rub the head of the misalignment, then apply fire to the head and each horn, and behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you have more trouble, and the body is moist and the pain is suffering, and the disease is outside, then apply four cauteries above the spine of the back; and leave it until the most painful part is healed, and remove your hand; afterwards, cure until they are healthy, and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cauterization except for that which is fleamatic, and it is first necessary to modify the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the pains are great and suffering from painful medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot suffer, make them gargle and chew often with good meat; then let the chief be in the middle, and do the cauterization as we have said before, and the cauterization on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the pains are outside and painful, do cauterization as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is severe, then apply the delicate cauterization as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture and fluid is large, then use the cauterization of parts as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is declining towards melancholy, and the corpse is wet with the painful moisture, then give it a drink of something by which the brain is cleansed, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After relieving the painful part; then apply a well-made bandage, like a circle, and put it on the head; and if the pains are crossed, and are held firmly from all parts; then present the linen, and use butter of burdock old; and heat it gently in the fire, so that the patient can bear it; then empty the circle by inserting it into the head, and let it cool; and do this to the painful part once a week with different governance until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you have seen cauterization done by making several points all over the cauterizer.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the skull and then places cotton wool on it in butter and in goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye's opening
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the first sign of eye opening comes as I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient a clean thing, guarding against all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times a day on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that command him to turn his head, and make the cauterizer go over his head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples together, or one on each; and cover all the cauterizer with veins and arteries that are outside the skull, and let the cauterizer be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against blood clotting, and if you see too much blood coming out, then apply a cloth as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of the cauterization as you would perform it; and never once has anyone cautery or heated anything outside of the two lower bones.
dou cors des larmes	The course of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins, or below the arteries which are in the appearance of the main deformed; and one sees that it is superfluous cold flegmatic fluid, then make the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of this work: I cautery emmi the chief, and II cauterize above the II temples, and II cauterize outside the II bones; and if there is more, then wisely cauterize above the sorcil with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through the path of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat according to what we have said in the division, and it does not work, then drink three bad things against evil spirits; after that, give the head a good drink, and cauterize or apply the caustic olive oil; and make two cauteries with the caustic called «clavilis» on the two sinews, a little below the chin; and guard the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the caustic called «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then use the caustic of this caustic called «olivare».
de coi ci est li forme:	Of this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it is necessary to make two cauterizations on the two sorbips as long as they are; and do not leave your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that does not oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never the case that the hairs of the oiled ones are converted to pardens, and they prick at their base, and it is made on cauterizations in two manners: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the eyes on the paper of the hairs; after, sign above the eyes a figure that is as much like the sign of the moon as possible, and is the beginning of the sign among the hairs; then put cotton moistened in egg yolk and muscadine oil on the eyelids, then heat the cauterizing iron:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize slowly and gradually on the figure that you have drawn, until the curer sees that the paper is retreating, and the hairs stand upright; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three hours, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burn is healed; afterwards, treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come back, and the paper is softened, then begin the cauterization again on the same joint, as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and is even, and do not prick the hairs with it.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauterizing medicine of burning heat is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a piece of parchment in the shape of the leaf of mint; then take French soap and live quicksilver, each one separately, and grind them together well; and apply it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it over the form you have made like the leaf of mint, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the disease remains only in one eye, then cover it also; and put cotton moistened with oil behind the eyeball; and the patient should be in a healthy state and show his hand over the medicine, and press the pouch and the mouth all the times that the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, for it stings as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine at your own discretion.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the burn is passed, lift the limb up, and if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, still apply the medicine on top of the limb or the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are set; then put cotton moistened in honey over it as long as the wounds are chosen, after care, the limb of the sore which is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have the task of staying well within your work, by great care that it does not pierce with those.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs are pricked in the oil, then begin the medicine again on the one that is molded by the proper paper, as you have done before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the fume of the myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the needles of men are different in size and smallness, and according to what you are constrained; and do not be answered the right way to that one who is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize them in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head in your safe hands; and wet the bandages on his head between your hands in this way that it does not move, nor remove his head; then put cotton moistened with urine or vinegar under the oil; then heat the cauterizer which is nearby: and fasten it to the head as if it were the form of a pen of lead, together with the quell so that it be the cauterizer; if you see, if it is appointed from one head to the other, and if you see, if it is also like a tent; but all the same, this which is fastened is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it is opened, and the pus is removed and dried; and if it is closed, open it and remove the bowels; after that, apply the cautery very hot, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the neck, where your hand does not burn; and put the cautery into the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just at the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you can do it again, and then leave it for three days; after that, put on a moist cotton bandage in butter, and the care of the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass before it is healed, then put on medicine with a corrosive agent until the bone is discovered; and the king according to what he would have in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a certain way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To a fistula, and fasten the leg; afterwards put into the wound a subtle form of this, which is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make of the quantity of one drop; and hold your hand or the cauterizer firmly, and do not move the hairs until the plaster has softened and does not stick to its oil; and it is necessary to put above the hair a cotton moistened with oil in front of or behind: the plaster heals the leg of the fistula, and the healthy by a marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer pus to the sinew, and bring the fistula back to its proper place in the bone according to what is necessary in such a case.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cracks in the lips that are called "hair", and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in the previous chapters, and the treatment does not help, then heat the small cauterizing iron in this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient in those crevices until he comes just to the point of death; afterwards, care for the broken limb with clay until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has fermented and rotted and grown old and becomes a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not improve: then it is necessary that you have the fire cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula; afterwards, plug or puncture the fistula, and keep your hand there until the iron comes to the end of the wound, and behind the limb; and do so once or twice, after caring for what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if it is necessary to expose the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it does not help, then put the tip of a hot iron in your mouth; after heating the cauterizer in the form that you put on the tooth; and place the cauterizer deeply into the tooth, and hold your hand so that the pain feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and restart the cauterizer according to your will; after filling the mouth with salty water, and washing the teeth for an hour and rinse out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the tooth that was moving is fixed, and the gum becomes soft when it is stretched, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or there is cold or heat, and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to use cauterization in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a freshly killed animal, and the tip on an iron or brass spoon; afterwards, take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and moisten it in hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth firmly and hold it until it is cooled; thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in hot butter is placed on the aching tooth, and put on the heated iron until the heat reaches the movement of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery is made by heating a sharp iron or brass needle until it becomes red hot; and if it is too thin, it should not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cautery, because of which it will form a scab afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be gone the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fill its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then rinse it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery on the part of the head that you wish, and according to what you have available; and this is the shape of the chain:
des scrophules	of the chain links
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the chain links are wet and cold, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the fire cautery of hair from which this comes, and have two openings for the fumes to escape through the other part; and put the cautery hot on top of the abscess once, or as often as it vies with the edge of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and put above moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; afterwards treat the wound with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the skull:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary to first remove the hairs by medicines that dissolve; after that, apply cauterization at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn with too much heat but with a small amount.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the base of the spine, and let the cauterizing iron called "clavile" be used because of its shape; and cure the limb as we have mentioned before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the mouth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of the mouth are from cold moisture, and the pains have no fever or sweat, and is an old disease, then make two cauteries on the forceps in their eyes; and the other cautery is placed between the breasts; and let the cauteries which are called «clavile» according to the form that is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cauteries by gripping the entire cautery which is called «poins» because of the form that is before in the disease of the ears; and let the poins be just a few, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, the patient according to what has been said previously, and let the burns heal for three days in this manner:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the burns are lighter, because you make three times as much.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, let the hairs grow on their back and on their ribs; afterwards, relieve the swelling inside the tenderness of two fingers of your right hand; and if the joint is misaligned inside, then heat the burn cream that has two fingers' width in this manner:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	et cauterize the wound until it pierces just at the costal, and then bring four cauteries together; and for this reason, cauterization is made with the cautery that has three prongs, because the figure of cauterization is these four cauteries; and they are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is it placed upon this one nerve because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery perpendicularly with silk; after rest the pain, and do not move the limbs by length for as long as it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	If it is dislocated above, this happens rarely, then make a cauterization on the thick edge of the cauterizing knife, or with many cauterizations in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and is solidified by the moisture and is healed of the pains.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach until it is at its condition, and are multiplied by his vomiting, and are customary ways of cures that he does not profit from, then it is necessary that the pains be soothed above his back, and extends his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After applying three cautery burns with a small spoon, one after the other, to the clavicle bone, and two more cautery burns on each side until the shape of the cautery marks forms at three angles, and there is equal space between them so they do not touch when they grow together; and let the cautery be applied so that it pierces both parts of the chest, and let the shape of the cautery marks follow this form without twisting:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the cautery is too large in the stomach, following this form; and if someone has fear of this cautery, apply it by pricking and holding above the stomach, and then cauterize the entire cautery mark called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the care that we have had before, as long as they are healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain from heat and moisture and great swelling, as long as it is not forced out of its natural condition by excess; and the hairs are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help them much, so it is necessary that the hairs be left above their natural position; and the sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondres, where the neck of the ox comes; and there should be space between each cauterization the size of a finger; and the cauterization should be long and thin, and not press much with the hand at all over the cauterization; and it should be arsed so that only half the back is bent, and the hairs should be straight up; and if it cannot, then it should be lying down, and extend its legs, and lift its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cautery tools with a surgical knife, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and you guard that you do not burn the whole court, for you would make it harder all over; and that it does not come close to boiling, for the courts are very delicate there, and the skilled ones must see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the cloth: if it is in the flesh, it does not cause much pain; and if it is in the cloth, it causes severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	When this treatment is done, if the hairs on the patient's head are not smooth, then one should cover the head or the abscess with a cloth, and then heat the cauterizing iron, which is shaped like a spike, from which this is made:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the iron until the wound is healed, and it comes just to the surface, until the poison is completely gone; after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds as long as they are healthy; and it should be used by no one except those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be boldly attempted, and in all ways, it seems to me that it is worth leaving it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the fire cautery of the breasts.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should use the fire cautery of the breasts with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, and as big and long as your fingers; and grind it in oil, and apply the cauterizer to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the breast and the neck, and two small cauterizers a little down in the part that is outside the beard; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the spine, declining a little behind; and one cauterizer at the bottom, and the other above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the breast, and one in front of the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but apply it openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And the ancients said that no one uses a fire cautery like a razor, and they scrape it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and then the pain is as we have said about the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the pain is now deadly, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said about the divisions of treatment, and it does not improve, then they resort to three methods of cauterization that are all good.
