Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times vomiting comes from this treatment; and if it does not come, then apply it to the extraction with fine pincers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it vomits with the pincers, it is good; if not, then apply it to the extraction with a fine needle; and if it does not vomit by this, then make a small incision in the top of the ear or near the ear canal, and stop up the opening with molten wax so that nothing can enter with the needle; then remove it properly, for many times vomiting comes as we have said; and if it does not vomit in this way, then take a piece of cloth and put it on the ears, and put any instrument that is sharp at the point to make, and put a little cotton around; then press the cloth on the arrow or whatever else, and remove it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all of these things that we have said, then quickly cut the ear as soon as an abscess forms and bleeds, and spasm; and the manner of the cut is that you first make a small incision into the painful part of the ear, and extract the pus according to its measure of virtue, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the grease depends; and let the cut be as like a moon, until you come to the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it vigorously to your mouth; and the cure as long as it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small grains that are embedded and swell, administer extraction; and if it cannot be removed, administer the following subtle method according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make a small incision when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tweezers and saliva, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in the case of something that falls into the ear, it is necessary to use blowing and a large piece of old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie flat on the ear itself or the sharp part.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the wind, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many thin, long stones according to the length of your finger, and heat them in the fire; and place the hairs one or two pieces of earwax into the ear, and from the other foot, and strike with another stone over the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone after stone until the sharp is completely out, and thus it will all come out; and if you see, take the reed, and strike one of the pieces in the ear, and the other piece from fire as long as the most dry reed is burned; then make another of the other stones until the sharp is completely out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the animal, if it is small in size, like a mouse and similar things, proceed as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then minimize the extraction of pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, if you cure them as we have said in the division and treat distillations, and the treatment does not help, then look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with fine pincers; if there are none, then take the form of a hook.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And apply the narrowest bandage to the ear according to the amount of pain, then it is often used throughout the entire head; do this as often as all the vertebrae are visible.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not comply with the extraction, then apply a cotton swab around the head as I have mentioned in the stone; and if they do not succeed as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have discovered for the relief of vertebrae, and you will find them where to treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which you see the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or lead, not too thin for the small pores, and above overs to distill; and to press within the distillation with a well-made silver instrument for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see from your medicines in the cane, and the cane should be in the ear; then press inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperamentally until the oil is distilled or chevement from the ear; and the smell of the oil is inside, and it should be the distillations a little heated to the fire as they distill in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some swelling in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by swelling of a wound, or by a bone growing inside the ear, and this swelling never comes from within the ear, if one cannot see it; and it always comes from outside the swelling, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is a serious infection in many positions, and in this one, where one sees, it is necessary to put the ear with the bad pain in the sun; and look inside: if you see the appearance of an opening, if the work has all this space of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the gauze be placed in front and behind the entire ear, so it does not stick to the ear; if the opilation is made of char cloth or horsehair from the ear, then hold the delicate pincers and the copper lightly, until that char is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is placed inside the ear, then take a thin razor and slightly heat it on the fire, then place it where the ear is.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opilation that the patient feels gritty in the ear, slightly pierce it, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten with Egyptian vinegar.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not touch the wound until it is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose petals, and sprinkle sulfur powder on top; if you see the ear swell, then remove the tent and apply another tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it as needed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood flows out, soak a sponge and apply cold cloths to the ear, and use other treatments that remove the flow of blood which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the writing of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for writing on papers when they are wet and then dry: extend them with tacks and pincers, and the copper from its roots; then place it on the lead broken glass.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without removing it, the cautery lenticular subtle, and the cautery-maker after the incision is good; and many times they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Frequently come in papers of the eyes things that seem gravelly in their form and hardness, and because this disease is called "hail", and is an assembly of large moisture above and below; the workings are such: if the hail moves from one part to another, it is a light thing to know; then make the opening wide, then scrape each part slightly, then take it with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it without piercing the paper, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, it gathers at a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the inflammations restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is large and descending into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the splinter in a pair of pincers, and hold and press it from both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it causes no harm; and when the splinter is cut, pour some oil of strong salt, and cure the wound with what has been injured until the wounds are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is squeezed from the paper above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears flow to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they sleep on them, and their papers are outside their eyelids moistened by the exinach that appears in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint to your touch and feel the extrusion between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand; then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains extrusion from each part, then put it on top of it; and press on one side and the other so that the extrusion is assembled within the circle; then cut in the middle of the moisture at the sharp blade a slit not wider than the wound on the skin of the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the extrusion; and in many positions, extrusion from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take the piece of cloth from the entire room between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not press into the wound, that you do not come to all the space above the oil, that you do not harm it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, then slightly rub the wound until it opens; then extract as we have said, then wipe cloths in gentle and sharp, and put on the limb, and bandage well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break silence and put on to corrupt the moisture that is remaining.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the abscess, which is too hot, then the healer applies wet compresses until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born that are not natural, and are awake, if they harm the eyes, and bring about various diseases as tears accustomed and softening of papers and albugine, until it is caused by the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cauterization together with fire, or by medicine cold according to what is before or chapter on cauterization, and it is done or by incision and stitching or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary to place the injured part of the body in your left hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is inverted, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of the thread, and above the margin of the paper where the hairs grow between these hairs, and draw the thread above the paper, and return the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs, covering all the skin from the great calf to the small; then straighten the thread, and place on the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of a bowl, like the bowl of a mirror, and throughout it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you saw lifted the paper that is divided into both.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if the patient has skill in cutting out a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is soft; then make all the spaces above the two lines that you have marked, and begin with the large leg joint just below the small one; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs at the base of the root, then bind the one end in one of the two angles of the wound, then scrape off all the skin; then assemble the two lips into a seam of an needle to all the thread of fine silk, and suck out the blood, and let the superfluity of the hairs above the two edges to anything that is glued, if you see it done; and if not, if you have no care, then leave the seam and the threads just below three or four days; then cure the wound without sewing things that are dry and constricting, because the paper revives at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is dried (as they say of the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if in another way: and it is that you sign the paper in a figure that is as alike as the pattern of myrtle, if you have three threads according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply pressure evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or there is a thread, and place it in the shape; and the other thread over the big bone, and the second thread over the small one, and gather the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have marked, as we have told, then gather the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointments and similar soothing things; and never once are the hairs of the skin turned: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing on one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of the canes is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the thread inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the space is; and cope with the two questions of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly above what surmounts the paper of the oil, and strain the two canes from the two parties form; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the copper has one force, then heal it until it is healed; and when the wound is dressed, and if the paper is lifted, and they will not grow back the hair; and this is the form of the two needles that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The workings are such that you grasp a thin needle, and draw out the silk thread softly and thin; then assemble the heads and not the other thinly, and let the lengths of the threads be one palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly in the trap, and not the heads of the thread; then put the hairs on your skin; and so it is beyond the sun so that the workings are declined, for this is a thin and small working, then draw the needle through the entire trap at the root of the hair pushed aside, and let it pierce into the paper firmly until you remove it from above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the trap, and let the other hair in the trap, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out of the entire trap with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the bone is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then treat the bone with the same thread that you have ordered, until the bone becomes fully healed and you can see it through the oil; then tie the thread and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows on top of it. And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the sheep's wool, and raise it with the other where you leave it, until it is fully extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the healing of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the pride comes from within, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes from a wound, or a cut, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this is that you remove that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bandage it until it is healed; and you should only use in its care things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Because if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of sharp or high and seeds of linseed boiled, and some drop of oil of cloves, and there is wrapped a tent, and the care of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take heed that they do not sound according to their former form; and this work that we have said is only to guide them away from this disease, that they do not return according to their former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is called "akrazat" truly is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work is that you hold an needle, in which it has a double thread, and the char in the oil, and make it pierce from the left leg to the right, so that the thread comes out of both the char; then the char is placed above all the needle, and the covering is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper's shape returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the incision, and return the paper, and make two cuts inside the paper; and let the ones who have the two cuts at the angles of the incision you have made be together, so that the shape is as if it were a letter with no "Greek" (ie, not crooked); then remove that char, according to the quantity that its cost is from, of what the paper means, then add the two missing parts and thread them with a thread of linen; then care for what we have said about medicines that soften and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a cut or a stitch or cauterization, then it is necessary to make a plain cut between the hairs and the papers, and according to what has been said before; then clean between the two sheets of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very different in form, and the wise masters compare all their knowledge to see how they can make the figure return to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	and of the paper

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil. des voines des eulz	of the eyes'

de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If the patient calls it "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with fire and medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then put it in the place where you cut out the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the pus that is there, until the bone is exposed.

puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully and do not come out of place, and do not dislocate, if they are dislocated, then you must tie the pain; then clean it, then put on suction cups or heat to draw out the pus, then put on the oil and a poultice made of acid, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then strain the oil, and apply the plaster with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes have in their work; then strain it through a sturdy cloth, and start the suction again without hurting; then remove the suctions and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the eyes dislocate again, you must strain them more; then remove the poultice after the morning and night, and if you see the oil heal, it is good; if not, then start the plaster and cloths and poultice and suctions until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a broken thread
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the broken thread, then open it, and it comes out like a strong piece of paper, and is easy to see; if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the part below this above, then put another needle or where the double thread of the arm is; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the double thread of the thread and wrap a part of the cloth around it, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and pour some oil on the injured part; and leave it until the thread chooses with the cloth, then care for the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and once the wound is closed by the cloth each part of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs appear to be too long, pierce them with a thin needle that comes from under the oil, and remove the moisture and descend the hairs, and immediately enter; then extract them until they are clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the edge of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease that is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a blade that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp edge descending, and it is not a sharp edge; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit with the sore on the seat well-covered and straight, then take the chief between your hands at two parts, and the movement until you see the blade coming up to your eyes; then it should be hidden, and not descend and be disassembled in the light, and see the things as they were; and if it does not descend, it is a sharp edge, and if it does not descend from the blade, it is not well-covered as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the pain is between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it over the cornea of the eye and gently by the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the boil is out; and when it is out, then pour in the hot oil mixed with honey, or hot or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similarities of the oils in the division, and what is needed to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary for you to make the dislocated joint rest between your crossed hands, outside of the light by the sun, and with clean and tightly stretched oil; then place the oil paper at your right hand if the joints are on the left, or at your left hand if the joints are on the right; then take in your right hand if the joints are on the left, or in your left hand if the joints are on the right, the instrument called «almagda», or in your right hand if the joints are on the right; then place the point of the instrument above the crown of the oil at the larger end of the oil to the part of the lesser arm, then strike the instrument called «almagda» forcefully, and with your hand restored as long as it pierces through the crown of the oil, and feel that almagda is approaching the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the beginning of the space from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then place the instrument above or at the sharp end, then extract one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he sharp now sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if he sharp raises the second vein, put the thread with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, gently pull slightly around your hand and and; then put in a little bit of silk, and leave the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye soaked in rose oil and enough vinegar, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on top with enough vinegar.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the splinter cannot be entered into the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too far in front, but make the eye gentle, then push the splinter, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, compare the patient's sleep with the darkness in which he lies on his back in the dim light; and for all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition just before this time; then remove him from this same dark room, and test his vision, and see some things, and then return the bandage to the seventh day; and you should not do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate him, because the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess is ready to burst, you should let the oil out in front of the seventh hour, and give it what satisfies the abscess; and when it is calmed, if you let the pus out and put on its face a gold leaf or something to cover any light, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house little by little, and convert into its case; and cleanse that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who was of the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people do all kinds of things with it, because of which the needle is successful, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almsgiving, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure gold properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads of these are of the same subtlety, and the others in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the garment for the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No one ever has or will have garments of various colors, because there are some that seem like scorpions at the neck; and if there are such, or if there is a garment with a bad color, and if it has a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case, in those garments that are good and not enhanced, it is necessary for you to place the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the wine into those garments, and the others outside; because this corresponds to what you can support from the subtle spirit of one part, as long as you know that that garment is completely clean.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that can be covered, open it with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if it is a pustule, apply a warm cloth, and cut it as it should be; and if it is malignant pustules, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is not stained and all the poisons are removed, then pour or cleanse with vinegar and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not heal, and moisture comes to the palate, if it is not healthy; and if moisture does not perforate as it should, because there is a bone above, where the instruments do not come out to cut: therefore it is necessary that you go with a piece of linen slightly thick, and hold it in your hands, and have between each end of the space an equal or unequal amount; and put the bad parts of the thread in the wound from above, and pull it through the mouth; and often do this to the child at school, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the mouth with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and clean them one after the other as we are who are or thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that the hairs have not been corrupted by the new wound, then remove the son, soak in blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian eye salve, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the mummification process has removed all that remains of the wound; then place a piece of cloth on the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lantern, like a cat, and conduct it thus; and if you see, make a closed cat, and let the instruments plain for purging the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	for the sinew of the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises at the head of the neck, which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large over time; and for this reason it is necessary to cover it from the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put the fire cautery or the burning medicine on the wound; and if it is difficult to cover it until it is large, if it is hard, of pale color, and poor sensation: if you do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when it is covered once, great harm comes to the pain; and if the abscess is softly touched, not of pale color, and you see that it can be completely covered, then remove the pain and the cover without fear, and cure the wound of similar and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Because of the continuous solutions that come in one of these cartilaginous bones, which is very rare and occurs in few people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, then look to see if the lips are separated on both sides; and then stitch them together at a seam, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side or the other, then you must scorch all the parts that are not healed until they are, then gather the two lips together at a seam, and hold them tightly, and powder with dragon's blood powder and frankincense; and place the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and leave it until it heals through it, then treat the wound as an ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of the seam is such that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses inside the lips, hard and small, and larger ones; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut under each one, and take out the pus with pincers and clean every part; then apply the wound after the incision of broken glass, until the wound is not soaked; then apply ointment, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often toothache arises from the gums due to the old name "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps, and cover its root, and let out the pus or blood; then place on the tooth viper's powder, or other powders that strengthen and dry; and if the toothache returns after the incision, and often does, cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the tartar is gathered at the root of the teeth, between the gums and the teeth, rough and sharp scars; and sometimes the black, yellow, and green teeth and stains come from the gum corruption, and are also smelly; it is necessary to seat the pain between your hands, and its causes should be in your holy place, and remove the teeth or the scars as long as nothing remains; and thus remove the black, yellow, and green, and the jaundice and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at the first layer, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the tool, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth have different forms of tools for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the tool used to clean between the teeth has other forms than those used to clean around the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you are treating a tooth for its pain that you delay drawing it as long as possible, because this should not be done by anyone; for it is a substance very high just like that of which we have no excuse to draw.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is very painful, it is necessary that you be sure of the tooth being dead.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the tooth is relieved, and you should be careful that it is not a dead tooth, and draw out the good tooth; and in any case, the pain does not depart until the evil is extracted, for we have already done this to such saints; and when you are sure of the dead tooth, it is necessary that you scorch around the tooth on all sides; then move it with your fingers or subtle forceps at first and at first, until it is well dislocated, then firmly fix the forceps; and let the one who has the pain in your saint between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump out, take any of these tools and gently push it into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pus is; and if the extraction is subtly held by hooks, that it does not break when being extracted; and it is necessary to cover around the gum to discharge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and reapply the pain by the evil of the root with greater pain of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must guard that you do not act as the ignorant do, who, by their haste and audacity, break the chariots at once, and never mend what we have told; but bring about great disease through the roots that they delay, or through the chariot that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the dense matter is drawn out, wash the limb with wine or alcohol and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, use the broken glass of vitriol; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long points and large handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick members so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be sharp to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you must put a piece of soft linen cloth on the wound or two or three.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, then push the forceps called "alligator", of which the patient seems like a beak; and they should be made inside like a hook and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, it is necessary that you dig around the root entirely, and place the instrument called "althali", which is a spoon-like tool, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too large and does not break at once, and the root jumps out through the hole, it is good; if not, with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other forceps that are before in the region of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large needles, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is not to be broken, and it has many sharp edges; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease show, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach about the instrument due to the diversity of the cases, and if they break the cartilage or other bones, or if they hurt, if they search for the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but let him hold and remove; then restore the limb with appropriate medicines according to this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if he has all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot be made or filed: therefore, the razor; and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this tool which is shaped like a small beak, and it is similar to a sharp iron point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper coin is slowly and slowly placed in the mouth for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be removed, then the coin is removed with a small piece of cloth like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the copper wire used to make arrows; and in the tooth, slowly and slowly place the coin in the mouth for a short time, so that it does not move until it breaks; then scrape the entire surface with any sharp instrument, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, it is necessary to remove the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front aches, or by percussion or falling, and the pain cannot be relieved because it keeps moving, and you treat them with restricting medicines, it does not help; then you should restrict them with a gold wire, because the silver wire becomes green and rotten, but the gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the sick tooth between the healthy ones, if there is one or more, until you feel safe on the other side of the tooth; then continue the covering towards the part where you started, and gently and carefully tighten your hand until it does not move; and let your string be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the loose threads with a needle, and gather them, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that it does not bleed the tongue; and then leave it tightly as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, then tie another thread; if it stays, it will serve in this way throughout its time, and this is the form of healthy teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two missing teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth dies, if it is replaced in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and it does not interfere with anything that is wise and painful, and it is never made into the shape of a goat's bone tooth, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is tied as we have said, and it stays and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to copper the tongue's tie
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There are no times when this tie comes from the tongue or by nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound burned; and the operations are such that you open the mouth with the painful tongue, and hold its head in your own, and relieve the tongue; then copper the nervous tie with the wide, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or not, and it is by burning of a wound, then boil the splinter and copper the wide gently; and be careful that the wound does not open too much, for the artery which is out; and when you have done, lift the tongue of high rose and of ease, or of high cold, then put out the tongue a linen tent; and treat the painful spots every night, so that the wounds cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If there is bleeding from the wound, apply a fragment of broken glass to the limb; if it does not stop, cauterize with a slow-burning firebrand, which is good for the wound; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see that the wound is of a dark or black color and hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards suppuration, and there is moisture, pour water through a narrow spout, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, apply a fragment of broken glass until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have removed all the blood; then lift the limb up and down, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never come from within the throat blisters that are called "godaths", and they are properly called the II amendments, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then be careful: if it is an abscess hard and of small size and of fusse color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, as for the outflow of blood; but let it be until it is soft, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check that the abscess has not moved and is calm.
