Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the painful part in front of the sun, and his joint should be in its proper position, and the work of the mouth and the jawbone between his hands, and press the tongue out from all the instrument, from which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass as some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the thread in the ammoniac, and draw it up above as much as you can; and take nothing else with, then cover the instrument with which this is the form, which resembles a forceps; and in any case the teeth are bent, one on the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use a pair of tweezers, with which it is shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, blunt; and when you have grasped one of the tweezers, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cold water, and if there is blood flowing, gargle the sharp pain with hot water, or use pounded green pomegranate skins, or mullein leaves, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then treat the cure until it is healed; and never do other abscesses than the two tweezers, so grasp them in that way.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged within her throat, specifically a small abscess; and she had almost completely closed her throat, such that the woman could not breathe due to the swelling that was choking her, and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been inserted with two fingers through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore immediately opened it, and inserted a finger into one nostril, then removed the pus through the other nostril, and cut out a large portion of the bone; then I repeated this process in the other nostril, and pressed on her tongue; afterwards I inserted the finger into these abscesses, and removed a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the woman was able to breathe again, and began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscess would then close up again, and fill the cavity that I had emptied, becoming very large; therefore I inserted a probe and cauterized it within her throat: thus it did not grow back; and I removed these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterward.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When referring to the eye, and it is protruding and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not too large and round, it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the section, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you must lance it; and the one that is rounded together and is not too long; and if it is bloody or dark red in color, then you must avoid the incision of the wound.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	There is great danger from the misaligned limb.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the method I have mentioned, you should place the misaligned limb in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument we have previously mentioned; then make an incision in the vein, and draw out the blood, and bandage it with one or two of the instruments I mentioned for cutting into the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not bandage more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you bandage too much, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have mentioned in the cutting into the two arrows, and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too great, then it is necessary to use an engine for the cauterization of the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of the cauterization is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the pain puts his head on your sound, and then press the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cauterization, and fix with sharp and live fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in using the movement of this instrument, of which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head has one hair or put the medicine, as the movements of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine over the vein; and the pain lies on his side, so that the saliva and muscle juice from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down the throat and the blood; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it over the vein, the quantity of half an hour, until you see the benefit and the medications of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument to all the cotton inside, until the cotton is burned over the vein; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry, and boil after IV or V And if you have the task of restarting the cauterization of the medicine, so start again, and after the cauterization bandage around the vein, with cotton greased in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be wrapped in sharp cold, and be treated with gargles until they are healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from incision than from cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and similar herbs, and all or some of them in a pot, and put vinegar in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the prongs inserted into the patient's mouth until the steam rises from the wound to the eye, until the wound is dead; afterwards, repeat often, until the wound dries, and guard that you do not make steam at the beginning of the appearance of an abscess, for many things happen; and do not make steam except at the decline of an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and place it inside the head, so that the mouth does not have too much heat; for the needle does not cause excessive vapor to burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, it has been found in the throat with an oyster shell or fish spine, or nothing at all; therefore, you must remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned to the throat, it is necessary to make vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is opened by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then it is swallowed; and when it comes back to the throat, it will stick, and then pull out the thing; and if it does not come out because of what we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the crooked instruments be bent at the head so that they can more lightly enter the throat, and raise the head high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that the instrument does not go there, nor push too much bone in; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, for it is easier or the thing is already there; if it goes down, or it pulls it all along the instrument equally, as far as it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinew
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the throat sinew, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the throat hairs to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sandal, then trace it with all the small nails, or with thin needles that are worth its weight.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, then take a hairy skin, and put it in the throat of the patient, then pull or move the hair of the skin, and do this often with the iron that is heavy.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient's wounds become infected all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it down to prevent swallowing, and move it to its hand often; and as soon as the sandal feels the cold, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not choke as we have said, then suffocate the bad smell of garlic, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of onions; do this many times, for it will eventually stop.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you hold a pot with burning charcoal in it, and place a cloth cover on top, and in this hole put the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the bad smell of the mouth under the chin, close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape but goes into the nose; and the nose will now cry out, and if she does not choke, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink any vinegar; and then it is necessary that she be cured by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the shoulder, so that when it can be seen, resembles a crooked hook entering the throat; and it has the shape of a beak, and there is roughness from lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the memory comes here after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncture and cut; and it is in two ways that one is in its own shape itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are at the chest.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the shoulder are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is ready to burst; and if there are others that one must pierce when they are ripe, and do not die as soon as they are completed, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and one leaves it until it is surrounded by pus, there is a chance that the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located deep within the limb, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located deep within the base, if you pierce it too late, it will not be able to pass through, and will remain long inside, and there will be a fistula; and it cannot be healed in the end.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to drain the pus from the perforation of the abscess that has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease in pain and inflammation, and the debatement and relief of the main abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation where the abscess is most dependent on the limb, and where it opens most easily; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no bleeding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the limb, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that, it may spread along the vein of blood from him, and is plainly full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and deepen in him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured according to the wide vein, according to what the limb has to do.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to treat small abscesses, small incisions; and large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the cure, and cover; when it has become as the cloth, and is softened, it is necessary to do as one does with bubbles: and if such are cut in three angles, and if such are covered like the fuller's soap, and other shapes and covers.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you lance them openly; and if the abscess is large, and has collected much pus, and you lance it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop the abscess on the other side, then do nothing else; do this gradually, many times, until all the pus is drawn out; especially if the wounds are of weak virtue, or women bearing, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never touch the wound until the pus has been drawn out, because by chance the wound may die, and you will not be harmed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, dry the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if a tailor complains, apply strips of linen or wool cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and much pus, it is necessary that you stuff each one with old cloth or shreds of linen to prevent moisture, and tie it just above the wound; then open, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flows from your work, apply sharp cold and cool, and wipe the wound, and put it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, apply governance and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is too tense, and if the wound or abscess is very painful, it is best to put on tents and clean cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a state of inflammation, and the wound is charred, it is best to put on clean cloths soaked in cold water, wine, or warm oil, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress it and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what should be done universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and are of various shapes, like the journals of a goose, and many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also fat and such abscesses that have moisture like chicken; and there are others that are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not involved.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the incision is that you try all the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	If it contains moisture, then make a cut through the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off the hair that contains that moisture, for it will return if you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian oil, if it is present; if not, use sharp and silk, and apply to the wound, and leave it there the next day; and this will prevent what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with oil that is suitable, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess does not hold much pus, then cover it with this form, lengthwise; and pour in vinegar, and scrape off the skin from all parts, and put on all your care to draw out the pus from where it is; and if the artery gives contrary signs, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And if the abscess is pierced, then cut and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And if the cut over the abscess is pierced and moist, then it is lighter, for it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or boils or has no moisture, and of these were the abscess or boil that I copied or from an old woman; and found the abscess also like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken; and if one had been pierced, one would have made as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Other abscesses coming or chief, because those who come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent joint, to let out the pus; and treat as it should be.
des scrophules	des scrophules
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there are abscesses at the neck, and they dislodge the jaws, and they protrude, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body, and they are very large, and they are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each abscess is properly within its own side, as with the one and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these abscesses are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and if there are evil ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good disposition to the touch, and resembling the color of the flesh, and silent from every part and not attached to the artery or the vein or the conduit, and not deeply embedded; if it is necessary that you remove it from above, and scrape every part, and stretch the two lips of the wound as one, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and that there is no spider web or tearing, that the hand does not escape, and do not see too much before, that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to close it, put in the wound vitriol broth, or some powders that stop bleeding, and bandage the wound; and let it stay until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then ask yourself if there are any small scabs remaining, and remove and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, it is not advisable to cut that scab at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through it without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove all the scab, it is necessary to gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then since there is no delay for excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary to cover the root of it and draw out the core, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that hold excess, pierce where it opens and dies; and pierce thus as before said, depending, then apply bandages and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well covered, if the cure of ointment encouraging char, until they are healed.
de squinance	of wobbling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I never saw one in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have wobbling, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and this cannot be helped because all the veins and the marrow of the injury are in those who have abscesses high in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the marrow, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it out in three circles or four, with a small incision across between the two circles or by the amount of the incision through the soft tissue, but not into the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis as there is no danger, and the vessels are long and do not bleed much.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the throat until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then clean the soft tissue, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the windpipe which jumps out through the bone that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it entirely with a cloth; then administer medicines that cause heat to rise until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stiff, and the pains are judged to be mortal, and the defect has passed away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should cover the epiglottis for this reason, that the pains cannot remain, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they commanded the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not coughed blood or bled from anywhere except her throat, the blood flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and cleaned the wound, and healed it until it was healed; and she did not die as long as she could speak, and she returned to her usual state; because I believe that in the lining of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called «hernia of the throat», and it is a large abscess in the color of a raisin, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or naturally without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is in two ways, one of which is similar to a large goiter, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a small incision in the neck, and the proof and search are throughout the entire intramural: if you find it as I have described, and cannot be removed at all, if it is covered, as one covers goiters, and remove it all together, if there is any; and search well and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	ourselves
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways of doing things, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell the difference that is between us and the issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is cold and fever lasting, until the blisters have passed, and is accompanied by purgation; therefore the fever and cold rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With our way, we have neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the blister, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large; and they are in two similarities, whether dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a new instrument, that you first try and inquire about it before any other tool called "entromissoire", according to its form as it appears in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you press or more moisture on the part that you trueve in the abscess, and return your two fingers slowly, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs through a cut, as it has color, make it so as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the wound does not come moisture, scrape off the fat, then make a cross-shaped incision, and take out the skin with pincers, and scrape off lightly from every part and remove the coat where it is stuck so that you take it away clean with the knife; and if you cannot take it away clean, tear it off in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if nothing remains, it often returns; and if it stays for a short time and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and hold the wound, and put on things to soothe abscesses, and treat other cures until it is healed; and if it is very large, cut out both lips of the wound, and treat what remains.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if it be contrary to you or another if it hurries and fills the joint with broken glass powder, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound heals, and remove the clotted blood; then return to the copper that was left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the shapes of the instruments for puncturing, and there are three ways: large and medium and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three ways: large, medium, and small, to reach the abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles that one buys for syringes, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and they cost as much as those that are already yellow, and they are more effective at drawing out black pus to reach the boils of fistulas; and they are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the diameter of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are nails with two teeth in three ways; and if there are nails with three teeth, and they are also in three ways; and if there are nails with two teeth, and one tooth nails, and they are also in three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these that we make are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except from one part, from which we remove the nails, because we do not want to cut the vein or the nerve; and of these intermediaries are the awls returned in needles, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and we use only one small instrument, similar to nail extractors for draining blood, according to this form, with which we drain pus.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back only once in its place that is healthy for veins, and arteries, and once again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, it should be according to this form of this line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing charcoal, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is greasy like women's, then cut into the ribs above, by similar incisions; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and bring what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, for the reason that the pains do not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the ankles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the ankles are hard lumps with cuts or cracks, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut along this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound, and leave it there until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat the wound with an ointment suitable for such a case until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofulous ones, then make incisions in them as we have said about incising scrofulous ones, and if the wound opens again, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the bursting of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is burst and the skin above it is swollen, then there are often abscesses, and just as much blood comes out of the vein; and if you know that it is for the artery, then make incisions longwise; and when you feel it with your fingers, hold them steady; and if it is for the vein, then make incisions across; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and angles and collarbone and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is at the head should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from arterial bleeding by pricking the skin above the long muscle; then open the abdomen with small incisions, and carefully expose the artery of the web, as long as it is not discovered; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle from the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not remove the flap that is between the two bellies of the intestine until the wound is healed, and if the abscess is in the belly of the vein, it is necessary to stain the hand with what comes from the abscess on all the skin, then remove the needle from the flap that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have indicated to you, or with the thread of one of the two parts of the needle at the incision of the first needle, and if you doubt that the thread will not fit, put another needle at the end of all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four, then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the wound and leave what is tied; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat the wounds and inflammations until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses also come in the artery and the vein, abscesses come to the neck when they are cut, or from too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these often occur in the joints and in all the limbs where there are joints, and this is very painful, and its color resembles the color of blood, and it is in many different positions with pain; and when one stretches it, if the pain increases, and it does not stay in place, but moves away from the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not need to cover them with iron: perhaps there is contraction; and those who are in the head or face, causing leprosy.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have a lancet, and cut at its root; and if it is large, if you hang it from its tip, and scrape, then remove the bone, and stitch the wound to the edge, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never found in bellies and never elsewhere, and is a disease called «funge» by the similarity of its appearance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and large grains; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or belly that were more like funges than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had small roots, and were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root; if the coping with the spatula wide, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often comes many great corrections of blood, and if you see the hair is spouting and painful from the incision of the iron, then take the thread of good quality, and tie the artelul as we have said, and leave it II days; then restrain, and do not stop pulling the thread of good quality until it covers the artelul, and cut through it with labor; and if the roots are large, then apply the coping directly to the belly, but you must well coping the half, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cover the flesh which is of pale color and poor sense and of light regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these infected abscesses, I will come to treat them with leechcraft later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the belly is swollen and hard.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from fire cauterization or cuts in the face, and is above the belly and has some of the pus, as it has in other wounds, or blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or inflammation; and if it is from the cut of the syphilitic sore and from the issue of the dysentery, then the color of the abscess is like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the end of the intestine, then it is the most diverse, and when one presses it to its place and it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when one presses it with the hand, do not constrain too much; and if it is due to an arrow, it is large and hard, and is like a boil according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the appearance of the work shows whether it is for the blood of the artery or the vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For it has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the bladder, then you must command the patient to dye his linen, and be extended straight out, then sew all around the belt; then command him to lie very still between your hands, then go around the part that you have marked with a sharp instrument, then extend half of the abscess upwards on the whole rib; then tie it tightly with a strong silk cord, and let the intestine be loose; if you pull the linen, and if you release the intestine, and bleed the intestine out of the lower part of the belly; and if you pull the bladder, then take it at the neck, and cut off the excess; and if the artery makes you go against, or the vein, then go around, then return to your work and take two needles, and take two threads of thin silk, and bleed the abscess as you have done in the cross that you will pierce; then strain the abscess into four parts above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the part remain until it can rot, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or you catch it when it has become thin and rotten, then cure the part as we have said; and strain out the pus or the moisture that you have taken, then cure the part as it should be, and soak the part.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the workings, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge once the evil of black bile; then make it clean if it has manifest repletion, then wipe the evil from the good flesh to do the working; then pour your needles or chancre, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow fully, and wipe well the place with your hand or any other thing, and if the blood flows again against the incision of the artery or vein, if it is cauterized until the wound is not stained; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the swelling is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only swellings; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarches, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look if the pains are weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as all and solution of vomiting and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has only dropsy alone, and he is neither too old nor too young, then thus: lift the patient upright over your hands, and the assistant presses the belly by leaning the swelling to the lowest part downwards, then take the spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be cutting of two parts at the point, and ensure that no part is so thin that it can reach the intestines when it is thrown, and cannot be bleached; then check if the hydropsie is turned towards the intestines: if it is for the disease of the liver, then your cut should be on the right side of the third rib three fingers above the nipple; and if it is for the mucous membrane, then it should be on the left side, and it should not be that the hairs grow over the cut so that the excess does not run to the weakest limb; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and press, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the face as if in scraping a quantity of an egg or around; then pierce the face until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the length of the scar, then pull it out, and close this instrument with this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or archaut, and has in its part not covered by the skin, small perforations; and on one side, three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the tailor cuts it like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribe makes to cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the awl, so that when the instrument comes to the edge, it should now be placed above the edge; without the half or the third part, because if you remove more than it needs in that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he falls palm, or approaches death; but in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound signify, and its thorns; then remove the instrument and retain the edge, and it is retained now for the one who stops the perforation that is above the syringe, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering so, and take a small quantity from the edge; do this every day, and guard against following too much until it is only a little edge.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and leave much of it uncovered, the cure for the sepulture or sand chafes, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and becomes tainted from drinking; and the cure for desiccative medicines until they are healthy, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the sharp object, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born without a wart on the rod, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick at all times very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or pierce the thin cloth subtly on the bottom, and tie it and tie him thus three times or four times, and when he wants to urinate, if it is possible, remove the cloth, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not convenient, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pierced is small, then he is treated with a thin cloth of the bottom, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the piercing in their foot are blue, because no one is born with the piercing at the top of the thigh, because they cannot urinate before their thigh is up; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come out to the marsh, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.
