And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie silently on their backs, with the head of the knife and the coping as wide as the tail of a pen, so that the puncture is made in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding from veins which often occurs, and if it does, apply the bandage that stops bleeding from wounds, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come blisters on the knife, and it is an appearance of a bad wound; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; if it is necessary to prick them at once with a thin needle, and to cover and clean all of them, then place on cotton moistened in Egyptian oil; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the inflammation is malicious, with a putrid color and foul smell, then you must apply heat.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the inflammation is inside the flesh and has part of it within the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the inflammation that is inside; and when it is cleansed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, if the wound is not healing, and becomes darker and more corrupt and pus-filled; then you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from the shells of grenadine pumpkins and vetch, then treat with other remedies until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization is helpful in two situations: when bleeding occurs and when corruption sets in; and if the patient's penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary to apply a piece of cloth soaked in urine between the head of the cautery and the glans, and piss on the wounds; and when the skin has grown back at the end of the cautery which had not been circumcised before, or if there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scrape off the affected area with a sharp instrument until the flesh is removed, and deliver the patient from the cautery in all parts; and if it is a difficult matter to decide whether to cauterize or not, then it is necessary to scrape off the affected area at the tip of the cautery and the skin, then deeply cleanse between them, and apply a thin layer of fine linen cloth that is cold, so that it does not grow back.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds; therefore, when we perform this work of our will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around the head, and with force, and in all one novacule; if it was the case that the two threads were not evenly placed and the one above and the one below did not meet.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the wound cleaning which is done by the end is not always sure at the tip of the member; and the wound cleaning of the angle may escape the iron, and correct the work, and many times it is born such that it has no need of cleaning and I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound cleaning which is done by force throughout the entire limb, I found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally through the entire body; but let the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and the method of the first operation is that you make the child think, if he listens, that you are only binding the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then throw it into your hands straight, and press the force between your hands or outside your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the rod and blow gently, and pull it up high until the part of the rod is clean; then clean the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it to the other limb; and take it as two in the second operation in the pouch and in the index, and cover between the two limbs, then lift the gently and pull out the head of the rod; then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on top of the powder glue a piece of dried bread cooked with red wine vinegar, seasoned with rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and treat the other limb as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for the anointment is such: the two hands should be tense and piercing, and the hands should be equally large:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the anointment is that the finger is too close to the incision; therefore, you should extend it to your elbow, and also the copper, and if you cannot hold it at your elbow, then use tongs, and then the copper.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they last for three hours, and what is outside the rod is inflamed, let it remain until the abscess is soothed, and scrape it lightly; and the copper, as you can move it, and guard against the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the patient of things soiled with wound powder, which we have said or treated for powders, and if it is done with excessive care, it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to the compression of a stone, or blood that has frozen, or a bowel, or a cow's horn, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not discharged, and you see the retention due to the stone which is in the bladder, then it is necessary to bend the patient's legs over their knees; and their feet should be placed on their back, and their belly stretched from the part above the back, and the stone pressed as much as possible; and thus the bladder is compressed above the stone, so that the urine is discharged, and if it does not come, then as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary to administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine silver hair, like the quill of an owl; and it should be thin at the tip of a palm's length and a half, and fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the end of a piece of wool or cotton, and pull the head of the thread through the tube; and cover the excess of the wool and pull it towards the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and the urine and the cloth moistened with olive oil and vinegar; then place the tube lightly in the cloth, until it reaches the root of the cloth, then double the cloth upwards over the bottom; then pull the tube forward just before the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming close to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except when the conductor or she goes is twisted; then the thread is tied to all the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and correct the urine; and restart the tube until the bladder is empty, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scarlet fever or blood comes into the bladder, and pus is assembled, and you see it distilling watery and medicines, then use all the instrument called «clepsedre», and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three points: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads by which the medicine cuts so that it stops well the urethra, so that they can draw out the moisture, and put as needed; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and pull at the end that is outside; if you pull the moisture to the syringe, and then press the end strongly; the moisture will enter the syringe, and come to the bladder now, so that it feels the pain; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that one clysterizes the bladder: if it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of lead, and it is the highest of the bones; and from there to the shoulder where the joints meet; then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see clustered in the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good woolen thread doubled, and heat the moisture above the fire; then pour the head of the poultice into the stick, then hold your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then tie the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the saddle, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with remedies; and I have said the difference between a stone embedded in the rain, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should make an incision; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder more often occurs in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles a sharp pain in its subtlety; and it has sharp pain, and great pain in the staff, and it happens many times, and then it returns; and from many of these jumps the foundation; and it is light for the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it is constant in those who are between middle age and old age; and it is a lighter cure for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it towards the outside, so that the stone descends to the edge of the anus, and never comes out of the upper part; then let it sit between your hands, cleaned, and its hands away from its thighs, so that the anus is completely turned downwards; then take and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not chase away the doughty one all at once, then moisten your right index finger with oil from your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull; and place it on the base, and strike the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the back of the anus; then press upwards on your finger, and cut where you see it tail off.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the anus with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles to his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin which is outside the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spatula shaped, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And making between what is between the ribs and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the right nave; and straight up the stone, and your tail should be at the foundation or the bottom, and straight through the cut so that it is wide by lack, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the tail that is at the foundation, that it would jump out of work; and if there is a piece of stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is gray to issue; and if there is a piece that is soft, similar to a glass, and rounded, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins where it should be cut, make the incision larger; and if it does not spring, it is necessary to strain it with pincers that are as sharp as a lime at the chief, for straining the stone so that it does not escape; or you can use a subtle hooked instrument at the head; and if you cannot engage it in this way, expand the small opening, and if there is no de-cortication, then strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be cut to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the place where the stitches cannot hold; but nevertheless you must try to draw, or tear with pincers, until you tear it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and put a moist cloth on top of the oil and wine, or oil and vinegar and cold rose water, to soothe the abscess; then replace the wound on its collar, and do not remove the bandage until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, let the joint rise well with oil and vinegar, then apply a poultice of honey and mustard, as long as they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is retained by the urine, which is known in a similar way that without urination: then put your hand on the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and destroy it; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and oil, and help it in all ways that you can, as long as it is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you cure it with, that you bind the two thighs, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is guided with a spoon, and pushed in, and the urine cannot come out; then according to what I said earlier, you should cut it many times, or excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod of this form and folded at three angles and covered in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the rod around the spoon, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the rod into the spoon until it reaches the stone; and gradually turn the rod in your hand into the stone until you can pierce it from the other side; then the urine will come out immediately, then press your hand over what is left of the stone that is inside the spoon.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is already broken, and has been torn with urine, and is splintered in the wounds; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then remove one of the bones from below the stone and the other from above, then make the rod in the middle between the two, then extract it, and release the bone, and clean the clot of blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare that stones are inserted in women, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who will expose herself to shame, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's, because it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if it is necessary to perform a surgery, it is necessary to seize a woman who is well skilled, and to point out where the true stone is, and if you do not know where it is, it does not matter; and present a sharp knife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command in the examination of the stone; and look very closely if the woman is virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her hand on her abdomen and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she must hold it outside her body, and recommend that she put her hand on her abdomen or near the pain, and press and move her right hand firmly over the vagina.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the body, where it is muscle-bound and feels the stone in that part; and do not move her hips above the stone or away from it, and let the tailor make a small opening in the belly, if you feel the stone causing pain so much that the stone can be removed, and know that there are many ways of stones: that is to say, small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round and those with thorns.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, put the wound in vinegar broth, and give it an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work, until the stone is fully out, and have instruments that I have told you in the extraction of the stone for men to help in your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and tenting and bandages, and do not restart, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, unless by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound healed, return to your work until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white sphacelus, which is outside the curd of the cheese, which contains the whey; and it is called «sphacelus», and never is properly in the web of the cheese, if one considers that it is another cheese; and this is the skin of the curd between the white sphacelus that we have said; and it does not have a pore.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is weakness that comes from thinning, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from impact on the thinning, and this moisture has many colors: or it is declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or aquous white, and there are more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white like we have said, then it is the abscesses, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the wounds, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own cloth, then it is the abscesses with part of an egg, and because people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the wounds and the white like we have said, then it feels good; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the previous forms.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes afterwards, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the hairs be cleaned according to the power and replacement of its body; then place it on its back, on something a little high, and put much cloth around it; then lean towards its right side, and command the minister to lean towards the left, and extend the lancet to one of the two ribs near the ribs; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the ribs from long to beyond the knuckle, and make your cut straight in dividing the skin of the ribs towards the white face, and scrape the skin subtly according to the power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp knife at a wide hole, and remove all the sharpness, and then put your tweezers, and press the white face up; and do not touch the ribs, but only the white face; scrape everything or even in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, if you do not scrape it well, it will return to the sharpness; and if the sweat suddenly comes to your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white face; then gather the two flaps of the ribs at a seam, then treat it as the other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you suspect the wound has become infected with another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are hanging, in doubt of the evacuation of blood; then cover the wound with a bandage, and remove the wound, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts together, which are two branches; then cover the other part as you have done the first evenly, then soak the blood, and put moistened cloth in rose oil in the wound; and put on top of that another moistened cloth in wine and oil, and put above the two bandages, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie it to all the limb that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and place them with linen charpie according to this resemblance and be assembled by sewing around the waist of the drawers, and one of the cloths is taken above the base of the back, and the other at the part of the elbow; and the other head above the two angles, and everything assembled is restricted in the loop of the drawers; and never is this branch of cautery in the form of an iron tail, and it is that you take one cauterizing needle fine, and cover the skin of the wounds, and be heated as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the acid is revealed; then take the cauterizing tool according to this form, and perforate that pus with small holes, and the skin with this subtle cauterizing tool:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	In all ways you can, until you have removed everything; and make sure the blade does not touch the bone; and clean this work to be safer; and guard against bleeding, and avoid injuring the surrounding tissues; and if anything goes wrong, such as an abscess or bleeding or other thing, treat it according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the pain is too great, and does not want to undergo this work due to its horror, then use perforation as I have told you; and when you are certain that the abscess has been drained, as we have said, place the painful part on the highest seat; then pierce the abscess in the lowest part of the wound, and make the perforation long along the body; and let the wound be wide enough so that all the sharp edges are removed; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it up, and leave it to heal; then treat the wound until it is healed; and if the white cloth does not stop the pus from coming out of the wound, it is necessary that you insert a needle or the instrument used to drain the abscess, as its form has been described before; then expand the wound, and let the pus return, and it will be reassembled after six months or sooner, and when it is reassembled as before, and thus the pain will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Because in the section of this chapter, many times I have seen more than one position, because it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the groin and also from the testicles; and it is due to many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive acid and ague, which is spread in the groin, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the blood; and it does not cause pain, and it is a severe abscess; and perhaps it is some gray and pale abscesses, and of yellowish color, and sometimes comes from an outflow of artery, or from inflammation of vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the presence of an abscess that is high and full, when you press it with your fingers; and you should only touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their appearance when gently touching with your fingers, and can often make a cut above this resemblance, and on other parts; and you should cover the wound with a clean cloth, then lift up the edge, and pull out the tube from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sewn with these stitches, then you should cut the wound and the stitch; and if it is open to the surface, or in the part that is inside the veins, then you should remove all of that which is held, and cover it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the arrow's head is in the back, then it is necessary that you cut off the entire thing, and extract the tip, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with linen moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the teeth
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	These are abscesses enveloped in an envelope similar to a bursa, with the softening of the teeth, and the pain is great when moving; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and therefore we will tell you the work of this, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to seat the dislocated part above the stable joint, then hang the suspensory ligament of the tendons down to your fingers, and all the veins that are close to the bone, and tie them with the master knots, and extend them evenly; then cut through the fascia at the narrowest point between the veins, until they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then take an awl or a double-threaded needle, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came from, and tie it to the other end; then puncture the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted blood; then cure the wound as we have said for other wounds, so that no vein is torn that belongs to one of the tendons; because there is no harm, and if all the veins come out visibly, it is necessary to draw the tendons from all the veins; so that he does not lose his grip due to the incision of the veins, and they dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the tooth decay
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are due to the section that comes from the tooth decay, or the extension on the stomach in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that decay to one of the coins; and this decay is either from the tooth decay, or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes: either from impact, or from jumping, or from shouting, or from lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs that it is from the extension of the tooth decay, are that it has little and little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal up to the front, because the tooth approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the cutting of the gums, that it brings about sudden pain at the beginning, and is various abscess appearances, outside the skin, and this is for the end of the intestine and the heart due to the cutting of the gums.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron, for which it is advisable to avoid.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the work is that you command or prick the intestine with your hand inside the wound, if it can be pushed back; then place the curved part of the knife over the collar of the intestines between your hands, and loosen the jaws; then place the curved part of the knife above the belly, and scrape all the skin of the intestines; then push the white intestine out through the wound, as far as it can come out; then scrape the white intestine that is outside the skin of the intestines, between the two white intestines that are outside the skin of the belly, and between the second white intestine and the part behind the belly, and between the second white intestine; and move the blunt end of the knife inside the intestines, and place the white intestine above your left hand, and loosen the belly over the white intestine; and command the assistant to extend the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the skin; and if you find any part that is not covered or white intestine, and if you find anything, push it into the stomach outside; then take a needle or a thick thread made of four strands of wool, and push it into the back part of the white intestine, which is after the skin of the intestines; then gather the threads together in the shape of a cross, and fasten them to the white intestine that is outside the skin of the intestines, with a strong thread of two strands; then cover the threads with the wool, and form them into two strands, so that none of the wool that is spun can enter the wound, which is not supposed to happen; and finally place the first thread according to the first thread, and then the other threads in turn, following the round shape of the belly; then cover the part outside the skin of the intestines, as we have said before; then apply a soft cloth soaked in oil to the wound, and apply the thread that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have mentioned after incision, due to fear of causing blood to flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has happened many times, and let the wound bleed until it stops; and if it takes too long to stop, then sprinkle with hot vinegar, and put on what we have mentioned, until it stops; then treat the wound with other treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done as the branch which is together with the vis, in a certain way that you tie the veins, after the belly slightly open; then cover it, and treat the abscess with what works, until the veins heal; and the treatment is as we have mentioned, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes a tear or anger so, as we have said, and open the wounds; and let no one pull out any of the intestines, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and in whatever way it remains too long in this point, the wound believes or syphac, until the intestine is pulled out; and this happens by the extension of the syfac which is at the tears, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and inflated the wound and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have already said; and in this way the wound is cured: and it is that the hairs are placed on top of their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the tear enlarged according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the syfac which is outside the skin that covers it, then take the hair and place it on the wound of the syfac; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds of the syfac above the head of the hair, and cut both; then pull out the head of the hair, and do not cover the syfac or extend the eyelids or other things, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you remove the splints, clean and dress the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scab is tightly adhered and does not appear to be broken, and the cauteries are quiet in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the boots is softened in some men, because the charred parts inside are softened and it can be seen; and when it is desired to cure it, one should first place the painful part on top of the softened leather, and then sew the two pieces together along a seam, and if you see that there is excess leather, cut it at three or four places firmly; then sew between the seams, and treat the wound as with other wounds until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Forcibly hold the patient firmly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is forbidden to hold the patient firmly in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the patient must answer questions when asked, and be cured by the same method; and the other is because we often have the task of holding animals firmly, such as goats and sheep and cats and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that holding firmly is done in two ways: by attraction or by puncturing.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, place the animal in hot water until the joints are softened and warm; then take it in your hand, until it is restored and you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the treatment of tail: it is necessary to apply a beast, and press the skin of the intestines with your right hand, then tie the suspensor, and cop over each eye at the top, when you have well burned them; and leave no drop of the subtle facial fluid that is on the vessels; and this method of treatment is more effective than that made by attraction, because by attraction sometimes something of the intestines remains, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is in two ways according to the second method: one is that between the two intestines open as the shape of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes it discharges urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and it is like a staff as thick as two fingers and two fingers long.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of the mouth and the foot is that you cut off all the infected flesh, and treat it like other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays from the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenting is infected flesh growing above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to wipe away the excess blood from your hand or from the wounds, and clean it lightly; and not to move too much before, since there may be more bleeding, then wait for the other cure until it is healed; and in another case that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and perhaps it jumps out, and it is according to the appearance of a snake, and because of this they called the old "snake disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you clean it as we have said about the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient if their nature is not well perceived, or their perturbation is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to them; or it is caused by a charm cast, or a subtle or sharp sword, and is made in the marsh, or on the sides, or elsewhere, and they do not conceive, and childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the aspect of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If their stoppings are near in appearance, then you should do it to your own or to the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle facial tic, and it is close to the two eyebrows, if you hurry, and do as follows: bring together your two index fingers, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two eyebrows, until the subtle facial tic is drawn out, and is over the upper eyelids; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the face, and grind the woman every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the facial tic is hard and sharp, it is necessary to apply a soft cloth similar to the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a horse's kick, place it upright and cover it with a clean cloth; and have medicines steeped in blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and an abundance of herbs; then apply a wide piece of plaster to the wound so that it cannot stick together; and thus let it dry, and then apply a tent of dry linen; and then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a horse kick, cover it accordingly, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually bleed, and when the hemorrhoids are old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when they are full of blood in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, if it is not treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then strap the altar as tenailles, and the cope at its roots, then powder with medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then soak her feet in cold water for an hour, then place her in very cold; if blood comes out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and peel of green pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take flour of wheat, and mix with honey and vinegar, and make an poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him sweat by applying vacuum cups to his back and chest without causing injury; then take the linen, moisten it in plantain juice or agrimony with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the affected area with hot compresses until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a sharp spike, so it should be covered as I have described the thelul; then continue treating it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from marshlands
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come from marshlands, such as chancre and pus-filled abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and pus-filled abscess and more other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must mention in this treatment the pus-filled abscess that comes from marshlands, which is not unlike other abscesses that collect blood; and if you have seen the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is engorged at the beginning of its appearance, and with heat and fever, and if it becomes red, then you should see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but make it wait until the pain is eased; and then place the injured part on a chair, and have two small stools where he leans, and support him on his back, and bring his feet together; and let his knees be spread, and put his arms out of his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then apply the bandage to the right side, and after that come the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument applied, that you check the depth of the wound, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the injured part; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument on top, and stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is done by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with a sponge leached; and when the wound is empty, it is necessary to put in the wound moistened cloths in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent from the wound to the front of the marsh, and place above the marsh and above the other clean moistened cloth in hot water or cooked herbs; then after two hours of poulticing, as long as it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then hot water or roots of lily and aristolochia are cooked; then reapply the poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sewn up in the marsh, it is necessary to guard against cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Midwifery is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman pressing down, and desire to smell the arms: then hasten the child to issue; then see that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press his belly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it descends on its head, then the second is with it, and is washed in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it never comes up from its feet, and comes forward the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes up over its belly, or sometimes, and is converted by chance onto its neck, and by other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the bonesetter to be skilled and subtle in these things, and if she makes a mistake and is deceived, I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes up from its head naturally, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and her strength is weak, then let the bonesetter sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and apply oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then blow the bonesetter between her two little fingers the small spatula that is in this form:
