et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And pierce the second one, and copulate with its angle until the moisture that is inside has been removed; and take the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not, then you must smear the woman with fenugreek powder mixed with mustard oil; then let her inhale and expectorate the condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now causes the child to descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, then you must gently and slowly reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then lift the chair onto the ground, and clean the woman, so she does not faint at the rising; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then copulate with the hands in the position that was previously put, and extract the child, and gently reset it.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it is necessary to put it up high; then slowly turn it and extend its legs slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps out of the cradle, command to grab and extend its legs, and let it sneeze with condition; if it jumps far, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come as we have said, slowly turn it and extend its legs until it is in a natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be immediately ready.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take musk of altee, oil of wormwood, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the affected part of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until beyond the ribs; and when she is thoroughly sweated out, apply a poultice of mustard, and remove it, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child has just been born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's head above its feet
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place your hands gently and gently; then place it on its back, and hang its feet down, and lie it on the bed; then gently fold its hands gently, and then grasp its hands on its belly, and remove its clothes off, until it is cleaned downwards; and if the child does not cry, then take its feet and gently move them, then gently move its belly upwards, then push your hands; and feed the child gently; and command the woman to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out widely with a hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then lie her down on the bed, and straighten her legs; then treat the muscle as I have described; and if she does not give birth, then sit her on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand; and hold the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command that it take a breath until the baby is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and it has extended its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I advise that the patient wash their hand, then gradually turn it back and forth, gently; when it is even, apply the muscle-stretching exercises of high and low, as we have mentioned, then command them to move it slowly; when you have done this, seat them on a chair, and command them to sit upright; and make them spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all the other fingers.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this for all the other fingers, grasp the second finger with your thumb, until the moisture is drained; and if the child's mouth can reach its face and neck, cover the mouth, so that it is not held, and move the child; then feed the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to sit upright: then it moves freely.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often the case that twins are born, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an uncommon occurrence, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if they are not named; I know that they are multiplied, and are devoured by the same sac which gives them birth, which is connected to the womb; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born grievously, as we have said the care should be, and if the midwife is subtle, and does it quickly and lightly as she should, then do it in such a way that it is worthwhile for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	There is no time when they are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, or seventh month, or more than fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise doctor, and it is necessary that the midwife knows everything, because by chance similar things happen to them; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you care for the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manual methods; it is necessary that you remove if the woman is of sound health, and has no accident or she is afraid of death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her knees raised; and the midwife applies two fingers, or she is lying in bed so that she is not treated with the extraction of the child; then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils mixed with mustard and fenugreek seeds, and linseed; then the midwife's hands with these oils and mustard; then put them lightly in the woman's vagina, then if she expels the child that is suitable for her, and if the child is born with its head between its legs, and if it is born with its head on its shoulder, or in its palate, or behind its beard, or in its cheek, or in its armpit, or on its back, then put the child to the woman's breast, and hold the child's head with your right hand, and place the cradle between your left hand's fingers, and rub it all over lightly, and do not put the child in any of these places that we have said until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the child:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then fish against the other tooth, where the root is thickest, so that the extraction is equal; and then move it equally from one side to the other, to help it come out, and hold the tooth on both sides as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, dip some of its oil into its two holes, and blow it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, place this tooth or higher up on the jaw, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back by tightening, it is necessary to wrap it around the injured part until it comes out; then cover it in the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus it is necessary to do in the other hand and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if the head is misaligned, it is necessary to use a tool called "almidach", which is shaped like the instruments used for this purpose in the following chapter; and thus, with great natural force, you must push the child's head back into place; then remove the bones with pliers, and if the child's head suddenly springs forth and is stuck on the perineum, it is necessary to cut through the tissues until the blood flows freely; and if the blood cannot flow, it is necessary to make an incision in the pieces that can be reached; and if the child's head is inflated in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is on his feet, then the attraction is light, and the advice to the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is on his belly or groin, it is best to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and when the belly or groin, as long as the moisture that is there; and if the other member is also affected, and the patient remains, then boil the rag in the mouth of the marsh, and pull it out from the mouth of the marsh; then boil the one or two, and remove it; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted due to abscess that has come, it is not necessary to force, but it is best to administer moist and greasy things; and the medicaments are emplausters, and sieve in high moisturizing and softening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the dislocation is above the shoulder, and you can put it back in place, then follow what we have said for the living child; and if there is no way, then try to pull it back with pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, follow what we have said for the abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be tightly bound, and other treatments should be followed.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other with that one, and the others also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the groin, and they swelled up so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the healer, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive, and some bones stuck to it, and after some time others did too.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in it were some bones, so much that the woman was in worse condition; and the woman thought for a long time like this, and then there was a little blood from the wound; and I do not remember this chapter except because when the masters find an unusual thing, they know how to give help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	For this form of pressure, we use books; and it returns to the two shoulders, and the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Therefore, the horns should be more subtle than the restriction, and made of flat or wood; and the mouth of the fust should be two inches wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be two supports of this same fust, which should be firmly held on both sides, half a palm long or a little more; and these two supports are placed in the mouth of the marsh when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of flat iron or boxwood, according to the appearance of the tongs; and it should have two joints, as you see, one palm long and two wide; and when you open the jaws of the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs apart, then push the two joints together into the jaws, and hold the head of the instrument between her breasts; then open your hand on the instrument, as you have done with the tongs evenly, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the instrument, until the bail does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all similar to each other, and there are many of them in their likeness; and when the one sees them matched, the more hurriedly the work is done, and the higher the cost for them due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disregard the instrument that you have not matched, for their need is not excuseable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is held in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the pain to hold her tongue, and then the faith is expelled from condition, and your hands are held to the mouth and nose; and if she sneezes through this, well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the pot, and make a hole or cover it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or cover in the pot, and the other in the mouth of the marsh, and let it steep until the vapors come into the marsh; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If he has a second attack.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment, and is not better, command the bath to wash her right hand in sesame oil or mussel oil, and then put it back in its natural position, and search for the second one; and when she finds it, grasp it gently and extend it slowly and correctly, so that the marsh does not tear at extraction; but move it lightly to the right and left, and then remove it; then it will come out and disappear.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the tongue of the marsh is narrowed, we have said the cure of expectoration, and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not have all that we have said, then guard that you do not follow the pulling; but it is recommended that what is at the tongue of the marsh, that you tie it to the woman's chest, then smear it with the ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it will bear and return, and come back; but nevertheless, when it bears if it comes badly to the stomach and the head, and whitens the pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is recommended to use fumigations of: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cresses and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to smoke the woman during retention of flowers and the second part is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is similar to a willow, and one places the head subtly into the fire, and the smoking occurs above the flames; and the fumigation over the coals, and the lice until they are destroyed, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but it has been stopped by some subtle swelling: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that swelling at its right place, and not pierce into the soft spot, and avoid touching the perforation; then put on a moist cloth with wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, put or plug a piece of cloth, and let it lie for some time, and be sealed as the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this stoppage of pus from a wound or an abscess; if it covers the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the piece of cloth.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodulated, and thicker than those that come above the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and shortens moisture above white or subtle blood, and never are these fistulas cured; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosity when the patient makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pass through the bladder, and through half of the urethra; and they reach the joint of the groin, and through the buttocks.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you insert your thin finger or base into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, then insert a thin tent of lead or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation, egestion, or ventosity as we have said: pierce it slowly; if you hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near the urethra, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the spine, and the tendon comes from the limb; if there is no twisting and the pain is internal, it is because it is stuck, and there is no cure by medicine or cauterization; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no other cure than labor, and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pain is hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to his knees, and his knees are bent towards his belly; then boil a tent of lead, or of plaster if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your index finger, so that it seems to have pierced the inflammation; and if you feel between your thumb and the palm, then cut out the affected area; and do not try to heal it unless it can be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is possible to heal some, but this is rare; and the aid that is done, is to heat the cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and push all of it into the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this twice or three times, until you see that these charred pieces are burned, which are similar to an arrowhead; then cure the wounded tent with burdock, until those charred pieces are gone, then cure the wound with ointment and bandaging.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If they are thus healthy, then it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, then there is no other way to be healthy; and if the tenting does not touch, and does not pierce just where it should at the base, and between the tent and the patient there is a thick covering of cloth or silk, and you see the fistula pointing towards the covering of the cure; if the copper begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes before the tent, and then the cauterization after, until it reaches the top of the tent; and he will be delivered from the tent, and closed; then wash away those cloths that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot move it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: it is to know, the burning of these charred chars, and the stopping of blood and the soaking of moisture; then cure the wounds with boiled or ground bread, until the bleeding stops, and the charred chars are removed from the wound; then cure the wound of the injured by applying dry charcoal, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from the base of the foundation, and is distant from the body, then press on the chest or foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the cloth or the syringe or the charcoal, where it is close to piercing, there should be no other means of support and hope, by administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it just above the base, or if you can put tents and cure it as before; and do not move too much in front, so that you do not cover the part that holds the foundation, and bring the discharge through the way of intention; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and wipe it when it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean that char taken from the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you put the tent into the fistula, it is where it costs the foundation below the skin above, so take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you pull the thread through, and put the tent along the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not possible to pull the thread through from the foundation below, then pull the thread of that which is pierced, so that you pull your other or foundation; and take the top of the thread, and assemble the two parts together, and hold them against each other, and let it rest for one or two days; and do not hold it at all until the thread covers those things that are between two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then I will perforate it in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too far from the opening.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the application over so far from the opening, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thread that is made for the fistula is very sharp and one-sided; on the other hand, it does not matter because we do not know what we should not do, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des worms
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Worms are according to two ways: either they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood, and some have a little bit of blood, and some have a lot of blood, and some have none at all; but those that are outside have very little moisture, and some have a little bit of sharp citrine or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the treatment of those that are inside the foundation is that you command the patient to sweat in other rooms until the foundation is completely dry, and the hair appears; then you quickly pull it out, and then you grasp it at its roots; and if the hooks cannot hold them because of their moisture, then you take them with tweezers or a needle, and then you grasp them, and powder them with any hot powders that are in the cautery chapter, or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, and then treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot be removed, then you cleanse the wound with a harsh and sharp paste to clean what is inside the foundation, so that it can come out openly; but if the worms are on the skin, and the hair is strong from the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you grasp them with your fingers or with tweezers, and then you grasp them, and treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and until it does not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to stitch the wound in this way: take a thread, and make it into a needle, and then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread away from the needle, and if it is too wide; hold the thread firmly, then release the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to allow for the excess blood; then put on the affected area a cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and put on the affected area, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and carefully where the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often found dryly and carefully in the intestines, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to scrape the surface above with a spatula or your nail, which does not let it moisten; then cure it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be cured, then start the scraping more forcefully than before until it is completely clean, and then cure it as it should be.
dou fremit	dryly heat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are a small appearance created before the heart, and it moves a lot in front; and sometimes it finds the frost, and one feels like death from heat, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a needle from an ostrich feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that needle on the heat, until the circle of the heat surrounds it entirely; then turn your hand to all around the heat, and cover it all in front, and extract the heat from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if you make a needle of rain or iron in this form, and it is thin from below and thick above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't touch it, to keep both hands steady, and press them; and if you see, burn the heat, as it is in front or chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the paste
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a paste of silver or tin, or melted lead or metal sheets; and never use small or large tools, according to those that are at hand.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those that are used in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large paste is above wide, or the belly is tied as follows:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a dislocation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the wound is on one side II perforations, and on the other I; and the belly or the one who puts the medicines in a beast's bladder or parchment, and perforate all around with small perforations, and there is between each perforation I must of space, then bolt in these perforations I filament of crushed thread twisted in X or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the tie to the instrument before a strong thread, then seal; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or wax or something similar, then press it lightly; then the assistant gives the patient both hands together until all the impurities are removed, then remove the poultice, and relieve the pain in the legs at the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in case of diarrhea, and the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the bandage is on the foundation or abscess, it should be as delicate as for a child; and this is the form of a delicate bandage over where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the care of wounds; now we will tell you about the care of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the limbs or wounds that are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from the piercing of a dart, and the cut of a spear or a knife, or a lance or a staff or an arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the limbs of the body, such as a wound that bleeds on the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the care of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds to the head, because its chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound occurs where the bone is not broken, and if it is a piercing or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of an abscess: if you do this immediately cleanse the wound itself if there is little blood from the wound, and cleanse the opposite side; and avoid the evils of overeating and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, let him soften his food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his diet; and apply to the wound, if there is an abscess, rosy oil alone or sterilized with wine; and if there is no abscess, put on fresh bandages over the entire wound that has not been moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if the wound has been moved, apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot come together by tenting, then stitch them together as I will explain in the case of abdominal wounds, with sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and can be moved but only held by a pin, then dress the wound with medicine, and restore hard char in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you suspect or find skin putrefaction and it is not near the bone, then cut off all of the putrefied part, and pour in horse urine, then dress the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein without clotting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find it displaced, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put this powder that boils as soon as it touches the wound.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; fresh sulphur three parts, and the powder finely ground, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it closes well and joins all its edges; then tie it firmly, and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use sulphur alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound be boiled.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but place above some ointments digested, or poultices of barley flour made with honey and vinegar, until it begins to heal; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fragment of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about the main fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fracture, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a fracture, there is no other method than to leave the care, and not put anything restricting, for it harms fractures and pulls them; and do not put anything sharp over the wound, for the substance of fractures is cold, and its continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be gentle, like lead washed in hot sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the bandage washed also in hot sweet water, and other pieces of cloth in this manner, and moist cloths.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then use bandages to cover it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and hairy and full of pus, prick or below the skin; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then cover it, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the veins, and the conductor is preserved, because the meat goes through it, if the vein is cut across the neck of the neck, and do not touch the neck but return it according to its natural shape; then slowly tighten it, and leave it for some time, then treat the wounds with ointments until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, try to remove all that you can, and what you cannot remove, leave until the wound closes and is healed; and if the wound is fresh, powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then the treatment as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from arrow or sword.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from arrow or sword, and the wound is deep, look to see if there is any ventosity coming from the wound that the hairs are not aligned: cut then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh at all its blood, do not put in the first hour the powder, nor tie it immediately for the blood that does not stop in the first place, and return to the heart, and cover the pain; but use attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put in the wound old cotton to draw out the moisture, and make the pain sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor trembling of the heart from anything else; and when you see the good dispositions, cut that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal the wounds of tents and other treatments, as long as they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then cut open a fistula; if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword cut, and it is simple, or small or on the back, then treat as directed; if it is large, stitch it up; if it is small, use powder, and if it is in the bone and has broken off pieces, then remove the fragments of the wound, and the others as they should be; and if they are not removed, let the wound fester, it will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. Belly rupture is great and medium and small; of the great wound, once the intestines or the nerves of the intestines escape, by which the introduction of food occurs; and the wound is more painful, and once the small wound is worse than the large one, because one must sew the intestines back in, unless they are sewn back in immediately; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel fullness, if they are sewn back in more slowly, and because the medium wound is worth less, because one must sew the intestines back to their place as with other II And there are four ways to repair a belly rupture: the two common costures are in the costure of the belly, and the costure of other body wounds and two other costures are proper to other wounds; and therefore they are more proper with the costure of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain each.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is injured, and it is easy to put back, this is done by one of the two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of salt in cold water alone, or boil it in cold water with vinegar and pepper, and cook the intestines until the swelling is softened; and never do this by restraining, and it is better to let it cool slowly.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling separate, if the intestine is moist with sharp or high and rough spines, because by this it is aligned to enter at once; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the tool used to remove worms; and the first care is to stop bleeding, which we should not cut without great necessity. And this is the instrument for cutting: it is cut from inside the intestine and outside, and remove the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is wide and the intestine has jumped out, if you can put it back in its natural form according to its own place, because this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located in the lower abdominal area, it is necessary to place the injured person on their back, with their legs raised higher than their head; and if the wound is in the upper abdominal area, place the head and feet higher than the affected side, so that the uninjured side is higher than the injured side; and thus manage as I said for large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply whatever is available to cover the wound, then place a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leaving a space of one finger's width from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread through both layers of skin. Then sew up the wound evenly, leaving a space of one finger's width, and insert another needle, tying it off as you did the first. Continue this process with the needles, as needed, until the entire wound is sewn up. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, as thin needles cover the entire wound, while thick needles cannot penetrate well. Therefore, the needles should be medium-sized. Do not insert the needles too far from the edge of the skin and flesh, so they do not puncture the wound before sewing. Then cover the needle holes with bandages or cloth to keep them clean, and leave them in place until the wound is healed. This method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it requires only one or two needles. When you have sewn up all four layers together, remove the needle from the part where you started, in the manner of sewing a shirt; and leave a space between each stitch equal to the thickness of a finger. This method is suitable for sewing wounds, and I sewed a wound that had been opened with a knife, which was over one inch wide, and exposed two inches of intestines, and was located in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with ointment after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in a place where none could be found; and I poured wine on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and the thread from the part before the skin; when it has pierced through the flesh in a straight line, then put the head of the suture or the stitch where you have inserted the needle, and let it pierce from the other side of the part before the skin; and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furriers make their pelts, and that you leave one side of the suture once, and then repeat it on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the sharp needles to the other head, in this manner: stick a needle or sharp needle near, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two heads of the suture; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part inside, the two heads of the suture; then pierce both from the front part inside, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of sewing and the best.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If someone says this phrase, and no one testifies to it, then you should sew the belly with two needles, or one in each; and you should place one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and it is said that when the tear is in the belly, it is sewn more painfully than any other wounds of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you clean the fresh wound with all its blood, provided that the doctor has moved it, then put back the intestine and the cloth; then put powder on it, and if the doctor has moved it, then put any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; then bind it with a bandage, and smear on sulfur and myrrh; then treat the wound as you would the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other duty in many situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, it is necessary to moisten the wound lightly with oil of warm temperature, or rose oil, and place it inside the ankles, and remove from the bones; and if it hurts or has putrefaction in the belly, and often happens, then clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and pierce within, and scrape as much as possible of the large intestines, which is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines that are called "jeun" cannot be healed when they are raw, and this is because of the planting of the veins that are in them, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the sponge jumps from the wound, and puts it back as the intestine when it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or blue, then you must tie the limb that is black, because there are veins and arteries in it; then cover what is between the limb, and hang the two sponges hanging from the part outside the wound to the end to align the extraction when the sponge falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of the boiled
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is broken and the wound is small, if it can be restored to some people, for I saw that some men were gutted from the abdomen by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became prolapsed and turned into a fistula, and in this there was egestion and ventosity; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the limbs seemed sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.
