And when I saw it being sewn up, I doubted that there were no bad things in his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and drunk and fed; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, one should be tied in such a manner: take a warm cloth, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the warm cloth has opened the mouth, place it on both lips so that it holds her mouth open; then cover the wound with another cloth, and hold it so that he cannot slip, then put the other warm cloth in that manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and over the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If this joint is burned in the intestine, and no harm comes to the pain, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in the following manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the head of this thin thread with the thread of linen, then pull the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and sew it back together; and this method of stitching is no further than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy or salve, only because of its thinness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Whenever a wound or abscess is covered and becomes generally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut open and let out.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to its hardness and whiteness, where one does not feel pain, and it is cut open like a quill of an owl; and sometimes it clearly opens out, and sometimes deeply; sometimes small, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, except by one of the EIGHT causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard pus inside and on the lips, that does not let new pus grow; or there is too much discharge; or the wounds are poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is in the manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and flowing out by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas that are made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to large veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the costal bones, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the principal member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas that are of this kind are of great difficulty in healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the joint that I have mentioned, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to treat it, then take a tent of tin or iron, if the fistula is straight, if the wire; and if the fistula is bent, if the twine d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well cover it with tents, then cauterize one of the perforations, for the moisture will not pass from one perforation to another, and it cleanses; then treat it properly according to your knowledge, whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is deep and covered with pus, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press on it, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or of nerve, or of artery, or of vein, or in any of the places that I have mentioned, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the cause and the corrupted parts that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply buried in the right place, then cut as much as you can, then put soft tents in medicine ague, and put them close to the mouth of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous part that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments of clean, sound charcoal, until they are healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves cause you pain or harm your main limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king boil it until the corruption is completely gone, then cure the things inserted inside charged with herbs until they are healthy; and if they are not healthy, and remain as before, then cut off that you are not allowed to go further: if exposed and wanting to be as far as you can, and remove all corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too far gone, and there is no other remedy except to leave it; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers, then extract it with the appropriate tool for that, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, and do not leave any; and if moisture makes it against you, and there is no error or fear, then use moisture and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them within an hour, put something pungent on the wound to prevent putrefaction, and leave it there until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, cut away the corruption until the bone is completely rotted, then close the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and comes close to the bone; if it must be so, cover all around the corruption, and treat it as long as it is putrid; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, such that the matter came to the leg, and was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open; but the healer by their folly opened too high that the abscess opened, and they drained much matter, and became a fistula, and there was much pain that everyone groaned and moisture of the body; and many more sought cure within two years, and there was no remedy in the art of hands, such that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were healing, and what was coming through the pores to great pain; and it became red the body of the young man, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one was coming into contact with another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hesitated, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from inside; I saw what appeared to be the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption, except that which I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with ointments for a long time, but could not heal it; then I re-examined, and discovered the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm's width of the bone, and treat it all over its surface, then I applied ointments; and it became healthy and healed tightly, and it did not need further treatment except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurs, but he was completely cured and born in the place of the bone, a hard char, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a piece of linen, and wrap it around the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended up; and put another piece of finer linen than the first above the first, and tie it above the char that is on the bone, and extend the head, so that you can remove the corrupted char outside, and uncover the char above the place where you see it should be, that it not corrode the char; and put a poultice or a cloth outside the bone to cover the corrupted char; and it should be done so that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the tooth is rotten, and not open, and the rot is in the middle or in one part, then remove the entire tooth; then apply a bandage from one part to the other over the rot, and sew the bandage to the long side of the rot, as we have said; and if the rot is in the joint, then cover the joint with the rot, and sew the bone or the part it contains from the other side; and if the rot is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way than to cover it; and if the rot is on the fingertip or the toe, then this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless it is necessary that you investigate this rot, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the blood vessel or the nerve go against each other; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare a tool for every kind of work, and know that the work will show you the tool that you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have to use according to what it should be.
dou feu	For fire cauterization
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The affected member will rot either due to its own nature or due to weakness; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicines, and it does not improve, it is necessary to amputate the member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes by death or by the greater evil, which is the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and then turns darker, as the corrosion spreads from member to member and takes hold of the whole body; if you delay in amputating, and if the corrosion is at the head of the member, then cut it off and do not give it any space for the poison to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the copper is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the copper is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do what you can when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, if the copper after the other joint; and if it comes to the bone, if the copper all the bone; and if it goes up the leg, if the copper at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than that the hurt will die; and the way of the copper or the cloth to hold the member is such that you tie it above and below, and on one side some ministers the one ligament below, and on the other side other ministers the other ligament above, and you disinfect the char that is between the two ligaments at the span wide, until the bone is revealed; then the copper or cloth, and put a piece of linen from each part so that the hurt does not touch the healthy skin, and it comes to the other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flows out when you are working, cauterize the limb quickly, or place some powders that stop bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded member with a bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my presence: he had a wound that seemed like burning by fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his right side, taking over the whole side; and when the honorable men saw the corrosion, they covered the wound, and was healed; and after a long time, the corrosion appeared on the other side of the hand, and it came to me, and I placed things that reflected after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he despair, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have not told you anything else but because of what others do, if they have business.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a wound that is kept too moist for too long, and it takes so long to form that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and remains under the skin, like a small bag; and the skin above is also as thin as cloth, and does not corrode the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus", and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the front, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is so thin that you must cover it all around, and especially when it is thin, like cloth; and it does not corrode for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the skin is hardened and the corruption is not yet in place, and the skin is charred, then the following ointment should be used: look to see if the breasts are large, and the nipple is smelly, then use the Egyptian medicine that is made as follows: take equal amounts of milk, oil, and licorice, boil them together in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take as much as needed, and make it into a thick paste or thin liquid, and apply it to the breast, and hold the nipple tight; leave the medicine on for two hours, then wipe it off; do this many times until the breasts are clean and soft; and no one should be treated with this medicine if they cannot bear the pain, or if the Egyptian medicine and the water of ashes do not help, then use the ointment of milk and melted wine, where the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the skin soft; and when you have done this, and you have confirmed that the breasts are clean, then use the ointment of rose oil and vinegar, and take some definite plaster, made with rose oil and wine; or use some other medicines and ointments, as I have mentioned their properties for treating wounds; and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the opening of the ointment cannot enter, then enlarge it with a sharp instrument, and put in an Egyptian tent or basilicon ointment, until it is wide enough; and if the wound is too large, then leave it alone, and let the skin or the ointment enter where it can, and if the nipple that is above is smelly, then cover it with a cloth.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowels are in the right position, do not let them hang down; and if you cannot cover the abdomen as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest point they can reach, for when the bowels are in the right position, do not let them hang down, and if you cannot cover the abdomen as you see fit, arrange it in this way: the bowels should move smoothly downwards, and nothing should be left behind; then apply consolidative medicines to the wound, and cover it with a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then apply forces to the edges of the wound and make them wider than the first, as they are softly supported by the other cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to align the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days; and whoever is on the edges of the wound should often remove it to align the bowels, and see if anything comes out of the wound, whether it is poison or a little or enough, or digested or undigested; and take precautions if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this way for some time and you see the nature that moves over the wound, then remove the bandage and approach the health; and then remove it in the morning or the next day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are too full and undigested after many days, cut them off so that they do not burst.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the subtle poisons are cut off after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take a long time to heal their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if the breasts become undigested after many days, cut them off so that they do not burst; and if the breasts are slow to heal and are far apart, use medicines that are moist in substance but dry in effect, such as oil of roses, and the same amount of old wine mixed with equal parts of honey; then cook it and use it; and the same is done with meat that is growing, when there is no oil of roses present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and the powder over the honey when it is on the fire; then apply the cloth to the breast, and use it once a day, and sometimes use aristolochia root and sky-blue lily, which is also like flour and centoire; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long and not healed by this cure, then cut out the corruption and make an impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the limbs; if the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the pouch of the nail, or the toe, or by chance in other places; and when it is opened, and no attention is taken, if the abscess bursts, and corrodes and drips blood so much that it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps corrodes it entirely; and then comes the corrosions up to the bone, as long as there is painful putrefaction, and the patient has a large wound, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, then you must remove all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bones are healthy and the joint is sound; but if the joint is close to the skin and begins to prick, and the wound, then it is necessary to remove the skin from the joint that does not touch the char, and bring the bottom up, and gently and lightly cover this char with medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it and drain, because as much as the bone rots and is, it cannot be healed; and if you see the other rotting, then cover it as before mentioned, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is fierce, and open, and it hurts greatly, then first heal it; then cover the joint with a thin layer of acid in cutting across, and make sure that the cut does not reach the skin that is outside the joint, because the hairs would feel too much pain; and if there is, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of a sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocations that occur in the hands of some men are all bony, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have a spike, and none of them occur at the root of the joint, or in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who occur in none of the fingers do not move, and those who occur at the joint of the finger, sometimes move; the length of the bony one is light, like this: cut it at its root into a wide spoon-shape.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who occur at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you have the copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must at the back nout, it is necessary that you first cut the round rod to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then cure it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in two ways come from birth or from the wound, or from burning fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut that which is sore, so that the one who owes it to repair according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, that it does not sore; or you put between two pieces of thin leather, as much as the ones are sores, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the patient applies pressure to any of his fingers with the palm, then apply the splint as it should be done.
des vils	of the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large and swollen, filled with excess melancholy, which come in many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never administer any clyster of honey, and then give the salve from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is that you apply it and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and let all the blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this way: first, the first leg of the high hot mustard, so that the big one is not subtly thinned, then straighten the leg with the bad one below the belly; then cut the vein in the left, or the second or the third, of a wide incision, then release and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, as much as the power of the bad leg can bear; then tie it, and command that he be cleaned with foods seasoned with black pepper; and then restart the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and not in pain.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The fire cautery is commanded to the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the vision is blurred and distorted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must torture it but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron that covers the eye is curved and does not cut into the vein; it is large in size, because if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but if it is large as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land; and by chance it may arise in other parts than the legs, and this has to do with the pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the flesh and bones, inserted between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there are signs of the beginning of this wound, which is that a very large inflammation comes into the leg, then the leg changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the wound is open, it is necessary to wrap it around a piece of cloth that is 1 and a half inches wide by 2 inches long, and the nose, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not present, if the wrapping is around the cloth, and the nose; and if it is too long, then take a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it will go back into the wound, and bring in an abscess and rotting flesh, and severe disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little from the top, and nothing remains or remains; and this wound never occurs when it is treated with 10 inches of length, or more, and some have come to me, which was 10 inches long, and when you cover it, it will burst or perforate, and pierce through to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and let the matter that is inside be drained, and administer medicines by injection for rotting every day, then treat the wound as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never again rain on this vein, and specifically when it opens into the joint of the little finger, or the big toe, and much pain comes from it, and it jumps back; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	lines of verse that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down the body, and is felt well in each member after member, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, as they come from snakes and leeches and tapeworms or intestines; and one doubts its malice, for as it goes through the body, and goes up to the head, and comes to the oil, perhaps it enters, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that the patient is curing and drawing, it cannot be otherwise than when it goes: therefore, it is necessary to hold the limb above and away from a very tightly wound bandage, then cut through and remove it, and if it comes out in front of the char, and you do not pull it out, then cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near to the oil, then hold it away from it well, then cut through and remove it; and it is necessary to use the poultice of healing herbs for the bad humors for the diseases, and if it is raw meat for purgation.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "windiness", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered one of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon afterwards, I saw it rise as if a worm were in the shoulder, more quickly than anything, just like quick silver when it cuts through leather to another; the pain departed from that arm, and went into the shoulder, and then a little afterwards it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she turned around inside the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how the disease moved from one member to another, for I had never seen it spread in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard that it could move from one limb to another, but I had never seen it in this way before; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry skin, and her veins were exposed, and because that kind of moisture appeared constrained; and it did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist skins and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain it causes, if it appears as we have said, then tightly bandage the affected limb and apply a poultice until that constrained moisture is drawn out; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the cause of that moisture, such as fetid pills, and serpentine pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the kinds of bodies they penetrate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are those that have large points, and small, and barbed, and smoothed; and those that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those that have pieces; and the one that pierces any member as it pleases: whether in a principal member, like the head, heart, liver, lungs, rains, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, shows up: then you must reset this arrow, for many die afterwards in various conditions; and when this bad sign does not show up, and the arrow is not completely removed, then remove it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and passes through the bone, and the tongue leaps up which is above the brain, are blindness and sore throat and vertigo and blackouts, and inflammation and blackouts of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without strength of the nose or the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are affected; and a white discharge from the wound resembling pus, and also like boiling water, and if these signs appear to you, then hold the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The symptoms of a broken bone when it breaks or shatters are that it is near the right breast, and also feels like it was stuck in something hard, not moving; and by chance the bone moves like a chicken's wing, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that does not heal is that without complaint of pus it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and sighs high and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrowhead is lodged in the quilt underneath, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and shortness of breath; and they move all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the stomach, by chance if it jumps from the wound, nothing of undigested meat comes out.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the abdomen, and it does not pass through the intestines, there is no hope of cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the bladder, and the urine passes out and comes out afterwards, and the patient feels great pain: it is a mortal wound.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, shoulder, and back, and the spine of the back, and the arms, and the hands, and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man who was shot in the calf at the root of the thigh: I tried to remove it, and took it out on the other side of the ear grease, and he was healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in one case, an arrow was shot into the oil paper outside of the skin, and the arrow was retrieved, and it could only be reached up to the tip towards the fist, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all of it iron without ears; the wound was sutured, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And an arrow was shot into the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I shaved the barbs, and carefully removed it until I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And an arrow was shot into a man, which was in his head or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, and inserted a probe, and removed it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a person who has an arrow sticking out or on their back, and the wound was closed over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural position, and found no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to help another person who had an arrow sticking out in their face, and the wound was closed over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And if you remove an arrow from the man of the prince, the king, who had it stuck in his neck, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely removed, I was called to cure after it had been sticking for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I carefully applied a thin tent to it, and I felt nothing; but he felt pricking and pain outside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the arrowhead, so I placed some attractive digestive ointment on the wound because the wounds did not swell; and the arrows appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I then applied the ointment more often, and immediately healed the wound, and the pain lasted a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound by hand, as long as it was open, and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow that was stuck in the limb; then I poured more of that corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound until the arrow appeared visible; and it passed well through the four months, and then decayed since the wound where I had put the nails, and one of them on one side and the other on the other, and could not exit; therefore I did not stop trying and engineering in various ways of instruments, until I got it one day with well-made nails, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, so that I took it and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was healed by the wound, and the patient was completely cured of the pain.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you may place your care above what I do not say, for books cannot explain everything; but wise masters know many things, and know what is present and lacking, to find new work, and new tools, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the body except in two ways: either by the way they entered, or from another part; and the one that comes out by the way it entered is an arrow entered into its own sinews, and it has never happened before.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is ready and the issue is alleviated; and similarly, if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot be removed, let her remain thus for several days, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, perforate all around the forest subtly, until the bones around are expanded, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly's ventricles, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned above cause pain to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but let her remain thus for several days, because if the arrow goes towards the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone only, and does not come out by itself, and remains there for several days without causing any harm, then use the extractor.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be pulled out, then apply tar around it as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is hidden in the flesh so that it cannot be seen, then apply tar all over the wound; and if you feel it, remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot remove it due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then let the wound bleed until it is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow that hold it in place, then carefully break the part that is stuck deeply into the muscle so that you can remove it; and carefully break or pry off the ears of the arrow until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow when removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the pain reaches to the shoulder, then cut it, for the extraction is alleviated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes it contrary to what we have said about the treatment in its chapter, then guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and proceed as you can draw out the arrow without risk, or quickly or firmly or strongly; and put the pain according to the form it was in when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then do it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place where one can see or feel it: cut then above, as far as the barbs can be taken, and then extract it: if it has now fallen.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, round your hand and insert it into the bone, expand the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, let it remain, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrow was inside, and you see that it has been administered gently, if you administer the instrument with a bristle, so that the tip of the arrow enters the bristle of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is caught, pull the instrument inwards to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is lodged, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces or sticks in the belly or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cut across, then cover the wound; do not cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then treat the wound if necessary; and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the needles used to extract arrows is similar to the beak of an owl, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the beak of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as in this case:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs for putting and for holding is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins that are common to the body, of which there are XVI main ones, namely: two in the ears, called "ear veins"; and two arteries in the temples; and two veins in the armpits, called "aspires"; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the back of the nose; and the two jugular veins; and the two veins on the neck; and the two veins above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the two veins outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins that are usually drawn are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the right side, and it is called "the great vein"; and the middle one is called "the basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and it is called "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the left side, and it is called "the belly vein", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one that is usually drawn, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the subclavian vein is the vein that is between the auricular and the annular, and it is on the right side; and in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: one is outside the corbeure of the pouch of the left side costeit, and the second one is at the ankle of the right side costeit; and the vein that is called "the jugular", which is at the ankle of the other costei; and in the other leg are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The first line translates to: "For the fire cauterization, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	For the first two arteries located in the temples, it is best to pierce them with a needle, and then cauterize them with an old, hot iron, and also apply a custom-made mixture of lime and tears to those places; and the quality of this treatment is as I said: that the hairs stand up so that both veins are clearly visible; and then the patient feels pain in the back of the neck, and then the head tilts; then lift the skin over the vein at the top of your index finger, and pierce the lancette outside, and lift the vein to the top, and cover it as you did with the other two veins, and treat the blood according to your need; then remove the pain, and place your index finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; then wrap it up and leave it until it is healed; we have spoken about this and its treatment and extraction, which begins the book.
