Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The healing of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the healing of cephalic diseases and facial ancient maladies, such as migraine and rheumatism; and the qualities are such that the pain is strange, twisting the head until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then relieve the pain by twisting the neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again from one wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it is not advisable that the flame be too hot; and the direction of the flame should be away from the bone, because the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The direction of the two veins that are in the two armpits helps them, and to the elbow, and to the wrist, and to the back in the oil, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their direction is such that the pain is strained by twisting any limb, as before; then the flame, and let the direction of the flame be a little farther from the flame, a little longer, and a little wider, because there is no harm.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, perhaps it will break; then apply blood clot, as much as you have skill, and then tie with thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood from the vein is good against the fever, and against sudden illness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and toothache that comes in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the pains strain their neck, then strain their neck with your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in front, and the sinus begins to bleed now; and do not move too much in front, and apply blood clot according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the second ingredients helps to narrow the veins, and at the beginning of the inflammation, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and in esting; and the quality of the salve is such that the pains strain their neck on one side and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pain, and the pain sits on one seat, then clean the vein with a long needle a little wide, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other side, then release the limbs gently, and hold the veins steadily, so that the pains do not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and chapped lips, and pain around the mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the pain disappear in front of you, and strain your neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore match both, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, match the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's dislocation
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The dislocation of the veins that are dislocated from the tongue helps after the dislocation of the cephalic, and it is by tightening the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sainier is that the diseases lie between your hands in front of the sun, and you elevate the tongue, and look at each side one black vein: heal both, and do not move too much, for from there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the side that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pinching all at once with a wide flame, or by thinly slicing, and it is called "aneurism"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of a firebrand is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is useful for opening veins that are deeply cut and contain much blood and trouble; and this is the form of a firebrand made of oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicately pointed, and is used to lance veins that are thinly cut, where there is thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The incision of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps in diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the chest, and where the belly; and it is necessary for the incisor to incise carefully, and to avoid the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If the artery is cut, and blood comes out, it should be cooled, as I said; and not be touched with the fire, but cut off as with a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, it is necessary to dislocate and change another; or you want any rain of it, or you clean in its place the vein with the arm: it opens clearly; and it is handled with fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the vein of the sinew, it is necessary to dislocate the arm as much as you touch the vein; then sign the vein with a needle, and then bind the arm, and handle the vein with fire as we have said; and beware that you do not cut into the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see blood coming out as high as a child's urine, and the wound is red and thin, then it is from an artery: hurry then, and put your hand longwise, then remove your hand without pain, which has happened many times; hold the arm still, and let it be so, and do not move the hairs until they are healed; and be in fear, and do not move it until it is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not bleeding, and you feel pain, and the medicine is not present, then cut open the artery if it is open, for the blood flows out; and stop the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a splinter of bread, and grind it, and take one half of it and apply it to the other side; if it does not stain, that is good; if it does, then cure it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stoppages are not greasy in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the little arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps to treat blood from above, as it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and the sauna must be done for all the vein that is out, and if it does not go too far in front, and he finds the vein, and he inflates and the grease is either greasy or cannot heal; and this vein often opens, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must use the sauna of the instrument anesil; and shield the vein from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it longer.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes; and it is best to puncture at the olive or nutmeg vein, for it is the safest of all veins, as it does not have any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to ask for the lightest vein, and do not hurt anything if it is not found the first time, and start again; and by chance, some men's veins swell at first, but it does not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healthcare is that it is not intended for anything other than maintaining health and preventing diseases from coming; and healthcare should be done in one of the three veins that are either cut: that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and if you should practice healthcare at the beginning of the day, in the spring and autumn, after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and if you should practice healthcare on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sane person who is administered for diseases does not have a determined hour, but rather at certain times of the day and in all hours; and it is not necessary to give sanctuary to children under the age of fourteen, nor to a pregnant woman except during the first three months after conception.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one administer sanctuary to the old who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one wishes to administer sanctuary in any way that is, it is necessary for him to cleanse the intestines of a light clyster if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous noxious matters to the principal members; and one should not administer sanctuary to those who are too salty from meats, or who are drunk, as much as they may be, or hydriopics; and if one wishes to administer sanctuary after colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent traveling, pregnancy, nursing, and whatever other virtue of the arm or body; then subtly the humors, as long as they are not too thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if one has them; then between or bath, if nothing prevents, to subtilize the sanctuary, and to administer it in the vein during the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day from work, from pain, from pleasure, and from similar things; and be tied and joined, and let the sanctuary be higher than that of whom one administers, and let the flesh of the arm be rubbed twice or three times, then strain the limb above a slow movement, for when it is too strong or weak, it cannot correct the vein; and then let him rub the limb with his hand until the veins swell, and feel if they do; then moisten the sanctuary with the flame of a small amount of oil, then put its due amount on his right hand above the vein where he wishes to administer, that the vein does not fail to strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flee as if they were strings at the slaughterhouse, and there are some that are plain from their softness, such that when one puts them over the flame, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if the slaughterer opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the slaughterman be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then one should try again a little lower or above, until the veins are no longer puffed up.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the joint is swollen and the pain subsides, leave it alone for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will form; do not enter water, then restart the healing if it suits him; and if the wound is small, or if you doubt that there is as much blood as you saw, apply a sharp knife directly to the wound; and the work should be done firmly, as long as the joint is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swollen, do not restart the healing, and put a little oil on it, for it reduces the flow of blood, and it is better than any other ointment in this wound; and thus administer the oil in every healing that you heal the wounds, to stop the flow of blood; and this also makes a triple and bowed shape, when it is put on the wound; and if it is too thick, separate it and spread it out.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there are large abscesses that often occur, even when it is not yet healed, only at this time or when the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and place a soft, moist sponge on the limb, and tie it with a cloth for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for several days without any discoloration or greenness, then you must not remove it; and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh mixed in a solution of camomile, monasterium, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the base of the church: place your hand over it, and if you feel the bone compressed by your hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place anything on it that we have said, for inadvertently you may cut the artery; but apply a dry bandage to harden the bone, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, let it bleed until it becomes thinned; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for those who are weak and have a wound, and for those who have a profession of arrow extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and let them be healed slowly and often, and they should be healed by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of healing is safe from the separation of arrows and the prolapse of nerves, and it is better than healing by a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those who have a wound on the body, it is appropriate to give bread moistened in the juice of green grapes; if they are hot, take out the arrow three or four times; and if they are of cold complexion, change the bread moistened in honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he pales at the sight of blood after much bleeding, then it is necessary to give him a broth of charred herbs and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to faint or bleed again, and bleed elsewhere, when he is weakened by much bleeding, it is necessary that he bleed a little and a little, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to faint or bleed again after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, then he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to heal on the other side, one must heal the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bleeds freely; then one must treat all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand on the pulse as it heals, so that death does not come in place of fever, and this has happened many times when the healer is negligent; and it does not matter much if one sees the arm blackening, and drawing out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that one presses firmly; but if it is spongy, one must extend the arm quickly, for this would be harmful; but let it bleed until it heals the second time; or you are not at the tip of the flame, so that the blood frozen in the vein does not come out, and put a small piece of cloth on it to stop the bleeding.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the swelling is evident, let it be and do not press it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary to draw out the blood the second time, if the healthy vein is in the same limb, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is healthy in the limb because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of the vein is that the hairs are pricked with a sharp, hot needle until the blood flows red; then it is gently moved so that the vein appears well, then draw out the blood through the cross, not too wide or too long; and let the punctures be large, and draw out the blood well near the joint of the hand, and if no blood can be drawn, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the hot water until you have enough; and if it is still not possible, do not repeatedly put the hand in hot water because more harm than good is done; and the drawing out of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the wound on the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and it is done in this way: strain the hand, and boil it in hot water until the blood flows out, if one sees it; and if the salve goes against the wound, and if you apply it to the whole hand, it will not hurt anything; and do not move it too much, for the nerves are all exposed to the bone, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary for you, put oil and thread on the wound to sew it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the right hand is useful for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the left side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophene is useful for all diseases that are not in the body, such as marsh diseases, and retention of flows, and disease of the rains, and of the coxes and of old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are that the diseases are quickly drawn out in hot water, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and tied above the joint; and the vein is at the knee, and through the joint many rains go; therefore, this salve is useful for a wide rain, or at the knee, which is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you find the healthy ones above the flesh, and the unhealthy ones are separated, and the healthy ones are treated as if they were sick; and let the flames be on them.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the flesh cannot be released, then put the flesh in the fire, and let it boil well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healthy ones must be cooked first, then start the second one above a little bit, because the first is salty; do not doubt the tendon, as we have said, and so make the other side of the meat equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The first vein of the arm is at the elbow, and its treatment is equal to the pain of the back, when it comes to an abscess.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in the bath, and it is strange above the ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and across; and it is better that you cover it, for the legs are clean, and it is very painful to others.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not straighten it, then he will have no pain from any that opens or does not open the vein, and towards the small toe, and keep away from the nerves; and draw out so much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put it on cotton and hold it in place; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is performed in two ways: either at full heat, or without heat; and suction performed by pricking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is at the top of the head; and the others are under the neck; and the other two on the sides of the neck; and the suction outside the mouth; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the hips; and the suction on the arms; and the suction on the legs; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered throughout the body, and therefore it does not weaken anyone, as is done with bleeding from a vein; and it should not be administered in any disease due to repletion, until the whole body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessary for diseases, it is recommended to ventose, or by habit, to ventrify every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each tense; for there are those who, when they have the need to ventose, have heavy breathing; and there are those who experience repletion and thirst in their face, and in their head, and in their throat; and there are those who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swallowed the tongue, and reach for blood; and there are those who dream, and see through blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is around the full moon, we order them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The fasting of the head helps to relieve the pain of the head … which comes from them, and it should only be done after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in place of the fasting of the cephalic, and it should only be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because this does great harm; and for this reason it should not be used by the watchman or those who have other cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often become unconscious, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little lower due to the uncertainty of unconsciousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vacuum on the neck is in place of the head and the chin, and therefore it is necessary to apply it at the narrowest point, and to the front of the throat, and to all, and to replacement; and it is necessary to place it only slightly, for if it holds too tightly, it causes unconsciousness or stomach pain and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vacuum on the two ribs of the neck is useful for head pain, and obtunds it, and emigraines, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the relief of the chin; and it is necessary to command the sick person to put his hand when placing it, that he does not press the artery, and does not cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilations of the mouth should be avoided due to diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the saints of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the shoulders are caused by diseases that come from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the elbows are as important as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and command the healthy one that he does not prick too much in front, for the legs are bare of flesh, and know how to draw out nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the back is useful for removing pimples from the foundation, and for diseases of the outside, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large and made of metal, so that it can properly draw out; and perhaps, if it is too delicate, it will break; and then great wounds are caused.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups are useful for drawing out blood from all over the body, and they relieve old pains of the rain, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and they remove the flours; and they are in place of the two knees, and the two ankles, and in any way they weaken the body after long use, and they cause pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is that you first apply it empty and quickly suck, then press firmly and move evenly, continuing this action until you see the flesh turn red and swell, and the blood veins appear; then stop, remove the cups, and take care of the body's position, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make wide wounds and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very sharp, you must strike the third time; and when we want to pull out the arrow a little at a time, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw out much blood, we should do it often; and if the wound is sharp, we should strike it from the front, and the end should be that the keloid is perceived deeply, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are hard, and who have strong pores, that you apply the points of the oil vacuums aperitive and dissolving: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or squash seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal, lily, camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balsamic oil, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to be treated has wide and large pores, then one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after steam venting with high rosewater, or high cold water, or mustard water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash or high mint water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluity rise from old wine, or vinegar of sweat, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be made to sweat immediately before the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep immediately after sweating, and it is good that they warm themselves when they should sweat and when they are sweated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	If those who are sweating are also feverish, and if they are too hot and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as large apples and endives and leeks at the side, and similar things; and they should drink pomegranate juice, and char of Castleton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little juice, and little pinches of pepper and pigeons; and on the day they are to be ventured, they should drink more than usual; and it is recommended to give some men occasionally three drops or musk before or after the venture, to strengthen the main members; and the powder should not be given to everyone, but only to those who are brave.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied to the body are those that are applied over the liver, and over the spleen, and gout, and over the belly and the buttocks, and the legs and the hip, because these members do not suffer much from being pierced in those places, and no one does it except to draw blood from member to member, as we put suction cups over the breasts when the newborn is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply suction cups over the belly and over the buttocks to soothe the member; and it removes the pain, when there is an abscess or stone, so it removes the abscess or the stone by its attractive power perhaps, and thus it does when it is applied over the liver and over the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for sweetness alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain hot water, as in diseases of the throat, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot boiling water, or hot water where there has been cooked harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction applied at fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two wide and half-palm-wide openings and a central small hole, like to put a needle, and it is of brass, and lead before so that it does not burn the skin when putting it on the limb; and it has in the middle a thin rod of brass or iron, for placing a candle, and they are big and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suction devices of children are different from the old, and the thin ones are different from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should put this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or liniment, and place it inside the suction cup at the end of the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the wax does not burn the hair; then place it on the limb, and do it as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor comes, and remove the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and repeat often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is used in the disease of pleurisy, at all sharp, there is no rod or stopper, and it is not administered except when it is full of sharp, and is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not removed except in members where one cannot place bandages due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, remove the clothing, such as two or ears, and others similar; and the quality of using them is that when you remove sansues that are in mild waters without pressure, take them; and put them in mild water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse the member with blood and bandages, then put the sansues on the member as much as it is red, and when they are smooth and ripe, and if it is a place where one can place bandages, place them, for this is very helpful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, first lift the limb gently, then firmly, well, and then wipe it; if the wound is too large after the fur of the hairs, then dampen a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the wound is cleansed; if the wound multiplies, then apply vitriol broken glass, or salves, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you place half of crushed beans on the wound, and leave them until they sprout on the limb, then it will stop now; if you have more, then take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the snakes do not want to take hold, rub the flesh of blood fresh, or you put a needle so that the snake bites, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick; and when you see that they bite, powder with a little aloe and broken silk, or ash, so they will now stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Be careful, dear son, that the foolish men see this chapter, as they have never seen any of the old books, nor read any letters; and for this reason the science is hidden in our land, because I found no good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that will be brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or prologue of this book the sums of the language and the chapters where the wise ones put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are uninformed may find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain comes to any part, it is necessary that you quickly clean the wound on both sides, if nothing else, so as not to weaken the body, or children, or the elderly; and if the tension is not very tight, or too rough; and use sharp instruments, that is to say sharp needles, and iron and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and use no heavy meats, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, so that you have no doubt of abscess or spread of matter to the member; if the wounds return to their previous government as they have used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one rub the thick grease of meats that make large grinding, or if it has viscosity, like wheat cooked in vinegar, and rice, and tests, and pie, and chicken breast, and eggs, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For grinding also causes pain and more quickly the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in the old and decrepit cannot be well restored or welded according to their nature due to the corruption of the members, neither those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset above the broken bone with large strong ones that harden and join the member together, until it enforces so as it was before; and do not let them all at once, and for this reason it is necessary to rub with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the breakers are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go through the arm, and others in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is broken with a wound, and broken all through a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own method, and its proper tool in restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and the break of the bone is known by the fact that the bone is twisted, and open wide from the outside, and it is to be pressed with the hand; and when there is no twistiness, nor is it to the touch, and the pain is not much, if there is no break; but it can well have twistiness, or cut, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it with your hand, but put on the remedies that come after this, and then gently hold it still.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the broken part that was torn away, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them evenly, as if incising an abscess, and if it is hot and comes, do not let any pain, until the incision is calmed; then gently and carefully put them together, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of that where there are pieces, then hold still, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	If the bone is broken into pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and at your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are joined, you join them together with care, and do not cause further injury or pain; and properly set the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it feels well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it heals beautifully, and do not strain it too much, or press it as those who bring it by their work cause swelling and contraction of the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is broken, strictly guard against moving it, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the member is so secure that it causes no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not broken, and you should put it in the correct position so that it does not feel any pain; and guard against it being placed incorrectly, as deformation can come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken member depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the broken member are different in size, greatness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as the arm and the leg, which should be wrapped with thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and calf: they should be wrapped with a broad and strong cloth, for the broad cloths embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it equally in all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap lightly around three or four times according to the length of the member, and hold your hand a little on each part of the cloth, then go above the wound and hold it less, than the wound gradually move away from the wound; and soften the cloth little by little, until you grasp a large part of the sound flesh, then take another cloth and return around the other side of the broken member; then return to the part away from the wound, and hold it evenly, neither too hard nor too forcefully, as we have said in the first part above; then place between the wrapped cloths a linen or cloth strip, until they are all equal, then tie everything together from above with a bandage, and then put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, put something soothing on the boil, and what removes the abscess, and leave it like that for some time; then place them under your feet, and be of equal size, one-half of a wide candle properly cleaned, or of wood from which the chips are made, or of palm rains, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the splint that you put on the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as it is needed for the limb of small size or large; then place them under the splints as you have done in the first chapter, then tie them together with a thread evenly, as in the first chapter on the fracture site; the tighter they are, the less; and it should be that the threads are of average thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and of flax; for if the threads are too thick, as I have seen in the works of those who make their threads of linen twine, and this is great error, because the bandage cannot be evenly placed if it is too thin, and it should only have about one-half inch space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the splints of iron after straightening them in their place, then put out of them a cloth, or other clean rag, so that it does not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bandages are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is not necessary to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put splints on them until after five or seven days, or more depending on your safety from abscess; and here is the way of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and you should take flour that is kept on the walls of the mill, and knead it with abundant water, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring fracture to many positions, and especially to women and small children, for it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of healing fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take aloe wood and ladani and enule and asafetida and Arabic gum and mugwort, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 5 grams; alechil, 8 grams; and make a powder, and mix it with a little honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it will quickly heal broken bones, and it is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of healing sprains: take mugwort and valerian, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 8 grams; acacia, 6 grams; and Armenian bole, 10 grams; pound them well and mix with vinegar or a little honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method to treat joints and bones that are dislocated from their places, and to alleviate the pain, and to use the bone to heal the wound and the fracture: take a new, soft linen cloth, and moisten it in warm oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not cure permanently, but it is good for soothing boils and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to cure broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of treating fractures of bones and to alleviate the pain from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of mallow, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are hot, mix with fresh coriander juice or vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of treating fractures that is stronger than the first, when an abscess is coming to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of mallow, and seeds of linen, balm, mint, and willow bark, and flowers of violets and camomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it with wax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it with dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to apply a plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and vinegar, and equal parts, and grind them, and make a plaster and the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then relieve the joint after a while, and be careful if the pain does not subside, or if the bone of its limb is misaligned; then do not relieve it by force again. If pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, quickly relieve it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and wet sponge with fresh sea water, and dip in hot, and lift the limb until the itching ceases, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with hot oil or rose oil, and tie with a bandage until you are sure of no abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then begin to apply the subtle poultice again, and a little bit of the previous poultice, and do not strain it as much as before; and subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plastering and of healing, then restart it as you did first equally.
