Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all as we have said, then do not delay in removing it for three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what we see, until the breaker is aware, and approaches the adjustment of the char above; therefore, it is restrained more than before, and increases its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb is drier than is necessary, then boil with sharp hot water every time you remove it, and this should be done every day, and loosen a little the binding; therefore, by this work, you prevent the suppuration in the limb, and heal it as soon as possible, what the foolish ones do, which torments the limb: it is bad, and if it is not done carefully, and only correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking methods
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are various breaking methods, and different figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by percussion of the spear, and the collarbone breaks the entire bone just below the face which is outside the bone, as if it were a wedge or a fist; and because of this method of breakage is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above through the side, and this method of breakage is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks, either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion embedded, or a cut from the edge of a spear, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone, which approaches the thread that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set in the bone as subtle as a small thorn, and the fracture is small, and because of this, it is called this fracture "hairline"; and if the wound that is made or by striking with an arrow, or falling, or similar things, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and the threads are like those of a cauldron when they are pounded; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens more often in those who have or are prone to moist bones, such as children; and they have all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are dislocated like these; and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the withdrawal above them, and the inspection of tents, and the corrupted char that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known because when one has revealed the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open fracture black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be careful of accidental harm, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any apparent injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractured bone comes first to you, and it is in the gum, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the state, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin around the bone has not been corrupted, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the broken bone comes close to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary to remove the part that is torn in this way: and it is that you pinch the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when revealing the bone, or an abscess forms, then help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with soft cloths soaked in red oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed down, and make sure that the blood does not come out; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in the second method, you have several different cuts, some thin and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron in one piece; and work lightly, so you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is outside and hard, it is necessary that you drill around it, also using drills with circles, but not so much that it goes through the tooth beyond the root, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the tooth; and you should have several, so that each one comes in its own place of the length of the tooth, so that you have drills for all teeth; and this is the form of the three methods of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To prick through the bone, it is that you put the needle through the bone, and turn to your right until you know that the bone is pierced; then return the needle a little later, and do so all around, then cover the incision the space of the bone between the teeth, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and guard that you do not touch the brain or the tongue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have the bone pierced and treated, it is advisable that you remove the remaining sharp edges of the bone to all other instruments similar to a needle, but it must be more thin and more subtle than the other needle; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Greeks say, which is much safer; and it is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open and exposed, so that when you have removed that part, you can place the lens-shaped piece of this incision:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the piece of this incision is in two pieces, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, then lightly cut the bone, because one cuts well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone's fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with the subtle razor that you must have in various quantities, to manage each limb in the most convenient way, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have large razors beforehand, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircutting and fracture subtlety, you should manage it according to its advantage; and this is a thing that is not replaced by anyone who has put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled two or three times, soak it in vinegar and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this more gently than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer other remedies from above, and do not pull out the cloth until the wound has healed completely; leave it in place for one or two days, until the abscess is calm, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lis roots, flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and administer liquid medicines without biting; keep the wound clean, do not leave any tinder, because when tinder gathers on the brain, it causes the brain to rot and causes great harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents occur, then if the patient experiences pain as we have said, it is uncertain with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no further harm comes except for the medicine that has been applied, which has its virtue, then you must apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one cloth, and place it on the wound; then cure the wound in the manner of curing until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sometimes the two bones above are broken, or one at a time, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small nail or needle through the wound, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the pouch by default, until the bone regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and guard that the pain does not feel through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot reach the finger, it is necessary that you place it on the head of a pin or a little thick one.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the broken part is of two parts, repair the other one, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then break through the head of the bone with linen cloths, if the broken part is in one piece.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you insert one or the other, if there is a break; and if the tents are so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no restorer that one should pierce the tents in the morning, and kill each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be pierced in the preparation of a plaster of egg and powdered mold; then leave the tent until the bone is firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never once open or nostrils with goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is a soft cloth around, and if the breaker holds, and blows the pains through; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put a piece of cotton or cloth soaked in rose oil or a little hydrogen peroxide on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come to the nose, apply a paste made of mustard flour and powdered incense, mixed with an egg yolk, then put light cloths on it and do not tie the nose tightly; if the broken part of the nose is small and broken into small pieces, use suitable instruments to remove them, then cut away the wound, and treat the other injuries as appropriate, and apply suitable emplastrums and ointments as appropriate; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents and apply hot compresses until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured without any wound, and the break is not completely separated, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather splintered within, if one knows how to recognize this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is in the right part, you should press your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left jaw, press your index finger with your right hand, and splinter the break lightly within, and bring it to the other hand by default, and make even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is divided into two parts, then it is necessary to administer traction of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the teeth move or break, then strain them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and place them on the broken jawbone, and place a double cloth over it; and place a large well-made board or a piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and attach it with a stitch that you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the shape changes, then release it to the beast, and then put back what is changed; and apply a poultice on it, of flour from the mill with plenty of egg or mustard flour, after you have removed the broken jawbone; and place the poultice over the emplaustre, lightly, and if the emplaustre adheres, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then treat it as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, wrap no piece of the bone in bandage; rather, apply substances conducive to healing with utmost care.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have healed all these pieces, and there is none left, then clean the wound, if it is wide, and apply substances conducive to healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the flesh
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times in front and behind the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is broken and disfigured in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the work is regarding the break with a wound, you should have two assistants, one to hold the broken forceps; and the other to extend the collar to the affected part; then set the break evenly between your hands, so that it forms as it should, without any appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round, flat ball of cloth or linen, and as large as needed, on the shoulder with the wound; and stretch and lift the forceps, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you can set the break evenly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder of the arm out of its socket, because it comes from above, then it is necessary that the hairs on the back of the shoulder be combed upwards, and the elbow is held in a medium position, and the assistant pushes down on the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the fracture to your two hands, and if you find broken pieces, it is necessary that you cut through them; and take light pieces, and if the bones cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but put the tool away from the shoulder to guard against infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	Seems like a spoon, and is not tightly closed, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, if you see, and one wide and the other narrow, as the tear in the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, if the wound is large, or you doubt an abscess, if the tear is small, use the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	For the breaking of bones, whether it is due to wounds or sawing, you should place a plaster made of flour from the mill and an equal amount of egg above the bone, and put light dressings on top, and place a sphere outside the fracture, if you have such skill; then take a very large bandage of one palm in width, then double the cloth over the dressing and the plaster; then take a subtle splint of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down; and place the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the collarbone, and outside the fracture, and outside the fracture, and splint each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture evenly, and you see clearly that the splint does not move above the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the fracture is healed, restrain it; and place the fracture on his back, and put a small bandage outside the fracture, to lift the injury upwards; if it aligns the shoulder by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the collarbone, and do not loosen it unless bad accidents do not happen, for about 20 days; then restart the plaster, if you see that there is such a need, and strain and leave it so long as it is restored; it is restored in the most cases within 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken or out of its joint, and it cannot be put back except by touch; if the splint according to the figure of the fracture, and the arm is put back according to its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with abundant water on the wound, and light dressings, and put a double cloth over it; then put a wide and thin splint, a little bit wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is not in any part of the shoulder, use strips of linen so that the splint is evenly supported; and then hold it tight with a big bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the wound every day; and every time it breaks, hold it again, and if it is out of its place, and bandage it again, and leave the bad hairs on the side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25, And when these numbers are completed, let go, and be careful, for this is not bone that can be put back firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is broken off before the joint, and not removed from the wound, then cut it out, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the fingers to relieve abscess pain.
de la brisure dou pis	of the broken finger
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fingers are never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it retracts from the wound, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of function, and all, and perhaps vomits blood, and the teeth are exposed in the broken bone, and the patient feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the painful parts are gently placed above their backs, and the metal is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades, and gather the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and subtly put them even in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and soaks above the thin salt sling, or other light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; and return the limb gently to its back, and gradually tighten it, and warm each hour with a warm compress, and if it relaxes, if it tightens; and if it is necessary to release, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the bone, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and release it, and remove the bandage, and address what has come from methods of healing; then reapply the bandage, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is important that the rib fracturer comes only from above, in the back, and at the top of the chest, and does not push too hard because they are sharp; and the patient feels it well during examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and splint, if you know how to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is displaced inward, it causes great pain and tenderness, as if of pleurisy, because the ribs press on the lung; and the patient must be carefully examined, and there is much blood and pus, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the broken bone back into place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, unless there is charring where it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then the healthy one.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that none of those who put suction cups on the limb for drainage is correct; however, doubt and there is in what the suction cup does not attract the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that none of those who should cover the limb with a woolen cloth in warm oil and then place bandages between the ribs to equalize the lung around it, then treat the cure of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that they cannot bear it through the bone which does not pierce the skin, and there is doubt, then it is necessary to cut across the broken rib on the side, and it is necessary to place a splint for the wound; and then one must drill the bone, and gently pull it out, and then suture the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with plasters, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the foot, then place moist cloths on oiled rose petals, and put on the limb; and treat it while the limb is in a position that is convenient for the abscess, and let it lie beside or on top of the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck bone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes the fracturer of the neck bones, and there is little that it rains; and so at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, if you take heed if their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you touch them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is often fatal in many positions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and do not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pain is cured, if you put care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, if you feel that the feet are soft, and if there are accidents that are in the hands, and above the back, there is a sudden ventosity and egestion without volition; and when it is placed on its belly, there is sudden egestion without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is placed on its back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is deadly: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess that is open, place on the spine rose oil or goose grease, as long as it is calmed; then place on one of the healing plasters and drying, and tie with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where you feel the pain, as long as it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover it with a clean cloth; then remove the bone, then gather the two edges of the wound, if it is large, into a seam, then treat the wound with ointment pouring hot char, as long as it is healed; and if the patient's bone is broken, which is called the "broken bone", if you have a bag of your right hand, put it evenly on the other hand to your power, then place the plaster and the bandage on top, if you have the skill; then tighten, and if there is a broken bone, do it again, and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, it is not often accompanied by much pain in the head; and making it long, and declining to the buttocks, and coming to the injury, and pointing, and swelling as it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the broken part; and cut away the broken pieces and the misaligned parts; and if the break is only at the top, then set it straight until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inwards, then lay the patient on their back, until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, apply the poultice, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part, so that it does not move; and apply the limb to the sides, until it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until it is calmed, and follow what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is located between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, one should restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a flat piece of even wood, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two fractured ends together and raise them high, and saw the painful part above the seat; then pour the broken arm over the flat piece of wood, as far as it can reach, and have a hook of wood in its place, then put something heavy or the assistant extends it below; then put the splint of the fracture together with its hands together, until the fractured one returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should prick the pain above its shoulder, and hold the hand on its neck, then command two ministers that one ties what is above the broken part of their hands, and the others tie below all the limbs, and stretch each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, hold the limb away from the broken part, above and below the broken part, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken part is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to tie the middle rope away from the shoulder blade, and the other towards the ribs, away from the broken part; and similarly if the broken part is towards the ribs, it is necessary to tie the rope lightly, without force, until the broken part is even with the shoulder and ribs; then set the fracture as it should be, and tie it, if there are no signs of infection.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it back for more than seven days, and put on it a poultice of milk and rose oil, until the abscess is calmed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you put the plaster on the swelling, then bring the arm up over the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and hold it over the shoulder, and over the arm, so that the arm is in place, without anything preventing it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, and have two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes three fingers on each side; then strain on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less when moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the straining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is not ready, let it lie for seven days, as we have said; then check every three days the wound, that it does not itch or swell, or the inflammation does not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the dislocation, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur within three hours or more, and the patient sleeps with his back, and his hands on his stomach; and places the remedy on the affected part evenly, and looks at every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the limb does not move, or the ligaments are not softened; then the dislocation is healed by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously mentioned, in a similar way that the food is at the first subtle; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg dislocations should be reset in 40 days after all; and then one must remove and administer warm water and medicines of oil for the limb to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the structure is deformed and twisted, it may take 2 months or more to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "forearm" bones, one of which is small and is the one that forms the wrist; and the other is large and is the one that is outside, towards the small bone; by chance, the large forearm bone may break alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small fractures are broken, the restoration is light and healing; and when large fractures are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If the small fracture is broken alone, then it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if the large fracture, then it should be more strongly extended; and extend it over the cushion, and tilt the palm of the hand higher than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the hairs cross each other above themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the hairs do not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers one arm to the part outside of their hand, or to the elbow, and other ministers to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no suitable bone to hold it together, you cannot restore it in its place, so do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaker there is a wound, I have spoken about it to the surgeon; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if there are abscesses in the beginning of the restoration, apply a poultice made of red rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and bind the poultice gently until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cast, and apply the plaster of powder from the mill with abundant honey, then place the splints, and set the splint of the fractured part further outside, and a little wider than the others; and it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the fractured part is in one of the bones, or in two; and it should be set higher above the fracture than other parts, and always less removed, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are above the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accident occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should raise the limb in hot water, until those itching are relieved; and let the limb rest without being too tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the reduction, and if the joint is dissolved and the bones are crushed, or similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tendons cannot come to the limb because it is too tightly bound, then you should slightly loosen it and let it rest for some time, until the tendons are corrected, and then reduce it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to harm, it will not last for more than twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Then, if necessary, apply your hands to his neck, and make his neck even, and guard against movement and flexion, and sleep on his back; and let it be known that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and possibly in twenty days, according to the compositions and constitutions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Let it be known that at the back of the hand and in us there are few fractures, and only rain falls many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plantar bone of the hand is broken or crushed, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place your hand on the extended table, and extend the surgeon's bones that are broken, and place them evenly in the mirror, as long as they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then put a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is in the outer part of the plantar side of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to bite on it at his broken foot; then wrap it with a long cloth, and place the splint as large as the foot of the hand, and hold it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outer side, it is necessary to place one splint above and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then wrap it completely around the hand, and stabilize the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the other two, if it is in the palm, place it evenly, as it should be; and stabilize with the sole, and if you see that you must place a straight small splint to raise the fractured part and not move; and if the fracture is on the other side, such as in the index or one of the others, place it evenly, and the joint with the healthy one that follows; or you tie them all together, which is best, or you place a splint above, as in the palm; and take care in restoration and arrangement of abscess, and take care of what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken ribs
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the ribcage are often broken, and one can see when they turn in front and behind; and the restoration is as one lies on the side of the fractured rib, and the other off.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs grow over its face, then each minister extends their rope evenly to their part; and this is when the break is inserted into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the ribcage, then one rope should be placed towards the nail, and the other ropes off the fractured rib.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And thus if it is near the knee, and then the ligaments above the knee are also affected, and there is extension downwards; then place the bone evenly in both hands, according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, unless an abscess does not form.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess, let it heal first, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the broken bone in two or three layers of cloth, and let the excess hang down, then turn the leg until the toes reach the root of the heel, and tie a long piece of cloth between the thigh and the leg, below the knee on the outside, and bring the end of the cloth up; then turn back up the leg and the thigh, and tie the broken bone with three bandages; then place the soft fabric between the leg and the thigh to equalize the pressure, then begin to bind in three or four turns above the fracture; and as you go higher than the fracture, and lessen the pressure; then feel the two pieces of cloth that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three bandages on top, then return to the outside at the top of the cloth, until you reach the knee; and the pressure, if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, then if there is no abscess or swelling, etc.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it is dislocated, and if you can, release it, and direct what comes out as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that you can grasp, then it should be left alone, if possible; and if not, then you must cut the limb, and extract the bone; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Never break the bone in such a way that you would put these splints on it, as in the dislocation and the arm; however, in the restoration of such a case does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And let it be known that the bone is restored at different times, depending on the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the artery of the neck
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	There are often many breaks in the artery of the neck, but it does not burst.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it bursts, it is only a small cut or tear, and it bleeds at all wounds, both visible and invisible, and it feels very painful.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting back what is torn apart, as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and if you have skill, place a round bandage, and hold it in place as it should be, then treat all the other injuries as we have mentioned in other broken things, such as abscesses and similar things; for each accident, put what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" by the right, and the other is called "foscile"; and it is as fragile as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the balanced arm, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg returns to its whole form.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is broken, it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it returns outside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply gentle extension, and make it even, and tie the fractures equally; but always, it is necessary to check if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and treat according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of linen that gird the leg on one side and the other, and are long enough from the knee to the ankle; then wrap them above and below, and tie in the middle as well, and at this point it will not allow the leg to bend to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long strips of linen, and if it is, and properly placed, and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot never break and they are few, and there is no other fracture in any position.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, if they are so misaligned that they stick out like a foot walking, then put your foot on top of theirs where the bones are lifted, then press them until they return to their original position; then apply the plaster and dressing above, and put a small roll of cloth under the belly of the foot, then straighten the foot evenly, then wrap bandages around it and other things that you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the joint is dislocated, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, set them as we have said for both bones of the hand; then put a splint along the length of the broken bone, and a bit wider, then put the bandage that I have mentioned, and strain it evenly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and strain the bandage from below the pied; and let it be above the head of the bandage behind the belly of the bone, so that it tinges well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident according to what is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are broken, if the wound is large, then spread it out, then incline it to the back part, and hold it from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then raise the woman, and lift up the back slowly, and gradually remove the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the wound, and the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has done so, return it, and do this for seven days or around: if the fracture is restored, and if you see, take a bladder of berries, and tie a cat to it, and blow all the bladder into the wound; then inflate the bladder with air until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in this way for some time, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice to them, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in many positions the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the wing, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert it into the wing; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or so inside, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleaned immediately, so that the cleanings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and the dressing of vinegar, if you have no other thing, then begin to restore the fractured bone in the same hour, or the next day, if there are no signs of inflammation.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if signs of inflammation come, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the inflammation is soothed, and do not touch it the next day or the fourth, for you will cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken jaw appears on the opposite side of the jaw, then you must gently place it in your hands and extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not properly equipped to be placed in your hands, then use an iron instrument that is seven or eight spans long, and its width should be according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mire to take three or four, according to what it has in each case of a broken bone; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not painfully press on the member at your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.
