And it is called "palainche," because the patient must have the broken bone placed above the top of the apparent bone; and it is hammered once, as much as it returns, and they are even against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is fine, and the instruments cannot well take the bone, it is necessary that you cut the top of the bone until the instruments have ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, then use a suitable tool, such as a saw or scissors, to your power; then grind what remains in the bone with roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the pain is great afterward, wait until it is back in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its natural place, then dress the wound with sterile black wine vinegar, and if it has been burned, do not put anything on top of the wound or any oil where it has been burned, so that there is no moisture and corruption; then administer these things as soon as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the entire dressing according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound does not become constricted with the breakage; many times the fool has done this, and brought on infection or death or rot at any time; and let the inflammation be less and more soothing than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no harmful accident has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain to the limb, then do not put anything on it; but wrap around it, in place of ointments, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to close, remove what you have put on it all, and apply an ointment healing wounds, such as Triple Antibiotic Ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be properly aligned in such a way that the bow can move lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the joint continues to move excessively, and it cannot be set but keeps dislocating, there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you suture the wound with a tent, and remove all these unnecessary pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if the sinus comes to the limb, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it immediately, for many times the patient dies, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The hasty blows that come during the cauterization
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Often after the health of the fractured bone, immediately near the joint, and the unpleasant thing is to see the appearance of the limb; and perhaps it cannot do its natural workings.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if it is fresh, then administer stiffening medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, either one or all together, and mix them with stiffening wine or with a lot of oil or with garlic; and place them on the nail in a cloth, and keep it tightly, and do not let it be in handkerchiefs afterwards; then remove it, and start another, until the dislocation is out; or hold a piece of plaster well made; for the property of the plaster is that it removes all swelling from the limbs; and if the dislocation has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the skin above, and make the superfluous part apparent; or you reset it with any saw until it is out, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after the garland
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, this happens for many reasons: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not loosened as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and could not come to the proper alignment of the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, then it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and give baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the inflammation often from high fever, until the swelling goes to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A misaligned limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is deformed, but it does not affect its natural appearance: then one should not believe those who say that one must break the limb entirely, and many have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps death; however, if the fractures and deformities are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs cooked, such as willow bark, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the mollifying poultice, such as diluted vinegar well made, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a poultice on it; or you take figs, and grind them with flour of coltsfoot, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation due to continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awake and hardened, like a stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, if it should cover just above the bone, make a thin, subtle incision; and put cushioning and rest in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned to its proper place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, if it is delayed, the joint swells, and if it is reset, it may be moved back to its proper place; for it does not matter if it is moved back when it is swollen: many times it brings on spasms and other pains; therefore, once it has passed, if the infection is soothed, then leave it until the infection is gone; then rise the limb with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it comes back to its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare that the mandibles are dislocated and the dislocations of the mandibles occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and a little softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If she is whole and complete, it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and not delay; and in such a manner that the ministers tie the head of the painful part, and push the wound slightly out of the one of her hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is outside, to hold equal; and command the pain to soften, his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the wound moves evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns gradually, especially if both jaws together, then raise them with high heat and oil, until they are lightly reset; do not delay the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned evenly, and the jaw with the bad tooth is well closed to soften, then put on moist cloths made of rose oil and wax, then lightly tie it with soft bonds; and let the bad teeth sleep on their backs, and their heads between two blankets, so that they do not move to the left or right, nor make any effort to chew, but take light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want lightly, and do not work much to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be reset to their original position within an hour and are not converted to their proper alignment, then it is likely fevers and sweating, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is a sign of danger; and many times those who have it die within four days.
de la forcelle	of the forearm
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forearm cannot be dislocated from the side of its own length and below, and it is not reset once dislocated, and well one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the dislocated part gently slides back onto its own length, and extends its arms; then press the joint firmly against your palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place; if the patient who is on the side does not dislocate, and if it does not dislocate again, then reset it to its own length as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until it is healed; and thus the same is restored to the shoulder, when it is separated from its own length.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder can dislocate: the first is that it dislocates at the part of the acromion below; the second is at the part of the pis; and sometimes it dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the arms; and many times it dislocates below towards the acromion, especially to those who have little strength, because for these it is difficult; to those who have enough strength, it dislocates easily, and returns easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they have a fracture or a blow, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by the bone.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must first examine it to be sure; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation is when it is down towards the shoulder, and it sets apart the sick shoulder from the healthy one, and you will find between them clear differences; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and below the shoulder the top of the shoulder, as if it were an elbow; and the limb cannot move its hand to its neck, nor move any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated above, if it is not hidden, for you will clearly see it at the back; and this kind of dislocation is only to be reset, when it is new, or if the limb is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministrants lift the hand of the injured one upward, then place their fingers below the joint, and pull the joint upwards to the shoulder; and the ministrants lift the hand, and extend it upward, so they put it back; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said beforehand, then it is necessary that the injured one's arm be soaked in hot water; and the ministrants should apply a softening and soothing poultice, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and it should be applied; then the injured arm should be placed on its back, and a piece of cloth evenly, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed below the joint, then place the foot of the injured one on top of the cloth, and lift the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the injured one; and other ministrants should wet the head of the injured arm, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now all right, and if you see that the dislocation is being reset according to this method: and you should make sure that the person who is stronger than the injured one is on the side facing the chest, and push the shoulder of the injured arm away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the injured arm hangs in the air; and other ministrants should take the hand of the injured one down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, it can move with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it can be reset in another way: and it is like this that one takes a long stick of earth, of which the patient should also be as the pistil, and not too heavy or rough; then it should be placed outside the pain, but with cloths soft on top, and the pain should be stretched along the long side of the body; then its hand should be extended from the other part firmly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a stick of two arms wide and four fingers thick, which has the head round to enter through the opening outside the shoulder, in this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the head with soft cloth, which was not the cause of the dislocation, then remove it from the dislocated place; extend your arm over the long one, and tie the assistance over the long one, and the hand at the top of the hand, then put your arm over the wide end of an arrow, and extend your hands down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in any way, it is necessary to remove the shoulder from the dislocation with an equal-sized ball of wool, then apply the poultice with flour from the mill, with incense and a little honey, over the whole shoulder and around, then remove the poultice from the dislocation evenly, and return the limb to the poultice, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change it little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then change it again after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and it is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is very strong due to moisture that has come, or for other reasons, it is necessary that you administer cautery at three points, as it is placed before or in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot raise the arm above, then cut the muscles at the head of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is by the ankle and the knees, or behind, is made by impulse and stretching of hands, and it is administered with another ointment; and care until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes swollen and moves slowly, then use the ointment many times until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and repeatedly dislocates; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired, for one can see and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, see the pulse clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is torn, and cannot move the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as the swelling comes, for if the swelling comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset completely, especially when it is at the back; it is better than other dislocations, but it causes greater pain, and perhaps it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to both of their hands; and their arms are spread out, and their hands are moved along the shoulder, in and out, and push the joint back together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the place, apply strong extension; and if two people extend the arm, and two people hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from both sides, then when you have loosened a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint at the hand, if any oil is used to soften the joint, then press the joint together, until it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on it, and press it together, and put the arm against the painful side, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bone, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the bandage and the bone, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is soothed; or place a piece of fat mutton lamb on the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove the bandage, and let him have a bath; and when he urinates, rub the joint immediately, then place the fat lamb back, and then let him have a bath; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then place moist warm chaff with butter on, and strain it over; if it returns to its usual state.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it must be quickly returned to its place immediately after it is dislocated, as long as the muscles are swollen, or if there is an abscess nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is done by placing the hand on a table, extending the fingers of the hand, and placing the palm over the appearance of the joint, and pressing until it returns fully. Then, you should check if it is properly aligned; then place the hairs of the hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the patient's hand on the table, and the doctor places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. If not, apply healing plasters and let it rest until you can begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot be suffered, and you cannot put it in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not use any force on the patient until the hand is washed, and nothing can be pulled out: then cut the nerve or artery; if there is no other means but to pull by cauterization through the skin, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have mentioned above, then strain and leave it for 4 days, then remove and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no swelling, boil some vinegar, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never dislocate both hands at once, never at the back of the palm or the belly; then keep the hand straight, and reset the dislocation to your fists until it returns, then support the back of the hand, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for 2 days, and then put it equal that day; and bind it as we have said, and remove the bandage each day, and move it, and reattach it; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	backwards dislocation of the shoulder
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck joint is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.

And the signs are that the movements suddenly occur without volition, and they cannot hold it, and often all the limbs are softened, or the two elbows or the two arms or one, and often the shoulder moves to the back; this is called «gilbositez»: the cure is that you warm the gilbositez if it came from childhood: if there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or from impacts or similar things, they said in the old ways of treatments by great words, which did not have much benefit; but I have abbreviated them according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gallbladder which comes from the left side, there is no engine or health; and also the one that comes directly in the second rib, and one cannot cure other than that proper one which comes from the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched out over his face evenly, and have some ointment away from him, so that he does not bleed; then make the bandage at the head in earth form, and the other at the feet, and tie one ligature outside the hairs of the wound, and the other on the buttocks, and on the groin, and on the knees; and the assistant should tie the ligatures, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the thumbs put over the spine evenly, until it heals.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a three-legged stool and place the patient's back against it, and the painful area should be on the side, and bring the head of the stool down on the back, then place the middle of the stool on the spine; and put the patient's feet on the other end of the stool, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the torso.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should tie two ropes to the head of the painful arm of one arm, and on both sides of the feet, and between each rope, on the outside and inside, a length of cloth; and in each rope, one knot to correct the twist, and the ropes firmly on the ground so they do not move; and between the two ropes, a rope turning around, following the direction of the limbs, and in the two turns, two small ropes of cloth of length, to return the twisted limb; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the other arm at the shoulder, and the other ligament to the feet, and each minister returns their rope to the whole limb, and the masters put the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a drying ointment with abundant oil, then cleanse and then place the patient's shoulder on a plank of three inches in length, to relieve the joint of the gilbosite and the part of the spine that is healthy, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle manipulation until it is healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing, then administer medicines to soothe and soften, with the ointment that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never does it appear in the back spine of the back, and one should not assume that this is dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, because one should not have any presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The only dislocations that occur in the hip and shoulder joints are dislocations only, not like other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated into four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside, and slightly misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of the dislocation inside is such that when the injured leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy ones, and it cannot double its knee to the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen with abscesses, because the cause of the belly comes from there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that these accidents are contrary to those previously mentioned.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has this in front are that he stands well on his leg according to completion; however, he does not double over with pain in the groin, and if they want to make him walk, he cannot do so before, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has this behind are that he cannot spread his groin, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated from the sides.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are that you should wait if the dislocation is recent, and it will remain according to its position, there is no cure; and there is no need for haste.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, you should hurry to return the joint, and extend and flex it, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you should apply strong pressure, and extend the leg firmly at two joints, or at one that is tied above the ankle; and some other treatments extend their hand above in a certain way so that they bite their hands from their elbows, then squeeze them with a belt above the hip; and others press the head of the bone; and they extend above and below all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat its similar case. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to support the painful side of the shoulder, then place the arm above the root of the armpit, and the limb that is outside the armpit, then extend the arm above the armpit and the armpit; then take other assistants to grasp the thick arm of the shoulder, and extend it in the proper form: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary to tie the two hairs of the shoulder together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the shoulder bone be extended two fingers more than the others; then let it hang from the top of a stick, and let it be two arms long from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the neck of the chicken, and let another minister hang with the shoulder, who can grasp the neck properly, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the back, then cut the hairs as we have said in the one with gout, and stretch the rope properly above the shoulder bone and also on the foot; then put two ties, one at the head and the other at the foot, then tie the rope between the chicken's legs in the correct form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not dry out, then stretch each minister towards it, and the master places the dislocation evenly in his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a flat surface, and press it as we have said in the gibbosity, and grind the hairs against the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg firmly, and as I have said; and place the fingers on the pain above the bent part, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the injured leg downwards, nor to lift it up, but it should be as it was dislocated backwards, as we have said in the prone position on both sides; and it should be on its face, and the ligament extended as before, and one must press on the joint at the table; and it will be right when the hairs extend their legs, and they will be even; then adjust the knees, and put the plaster, and the bandage of a cloth, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, remove the bandage, as before, and leave it for three days; then release, and make the member walk well, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and backwards; and it does not dislocate forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if they cannot do so at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend their leg if possible, and place your back against their face, and place their foot on yours; then take their shoulder to your palms, and bring it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and other ministers extend their foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the signs are that they can lightly bend their leg at the knee; and apply the plaster to the knee and thigh, and massage them firmly for three or four hours, then release it; and do not work on the patient again until their limb is strong.

de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never sprained, and never fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement. Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you should sit the pain straight, and hold it with the minister's hands outside the leg, above the ankle; then pull the bone to your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and hit the bone hard upwards; do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the bone; if it returns, it is good; if not, if you start again with the work, because it returns; and if it cannot return like this, then let the pain lie on its back above the ground, and firmly step on the ground between its knees, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not move the bone; then hold the minister's knee, and other ministers extend the bone to your hands or to the other, so that they tie the collar of the bone; then extend all the ministers equally, and the steps should be held between the knees of the pain to retain the pain while extending it; then put the minister's hands even with the dislocation at their hands, and other ministers hold the leg clean on the outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she does not go away, put the plaster on and soak it above, and let the swelling form, and tie the leg to the foot, and hold the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints are not too stretched; then leave it for two or three days, and if the joints dislocate again, apply the plaster again; then release it on the third or fourth day, and let it walk for four days; and if it goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, it is necessary that you ease them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they are not too far apart, it is a simple matter to extend them with work.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any way out of place, it is necessary to sit the misaligned bone straight on a flat or level table, and put your foot on what opens up these jointures, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; when it is even, and there is no opening, put some oil on the sole of your foot, then stretch it firmly for three hours, then release; let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocations, and one wants to restore them, often times the pain is fatal: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and do not know the art well, and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and slow, and not harsh; at the beginning of things, calm the swelling abscess, and leave the pain in the hands of God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place, as long as the swelling goes away; and when the member is in place, administer calming remedies for the swelling, and cure the wound, as it should be, with drying agents; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are shattered, remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into the path of fear, according to what I have said, for this is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
Amen	Amen
